Resolving Disputes on Conditional Divorce: Husband's Word Prevails
Rule for resolving conflict between spouses on condition occurrence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for resolving a dispute between spouses over the occurrence of a condition in a conditional divorce and apply the principles of asl (default presumption) and burden of proof to similar evidentiary scenarios.

Core Idea
The original state is non-occurrence; the husband as defendant is believed unless the wife provides evidence.

In marital disputes over whether a condition for divorce actually occurred, who should the judge believe? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi rule: the husband's word is taken as true unless the wife can produce witnesses. The principle rests on the legal maxim of asl (original state) and the allocation of burden of proof to the claimant. Understanding this ruling helps you see how Islamic evidence law protects the default status quo and places the duty to prove any change on the one asserting it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The passage deals with a scenario: the husband says the condition (e.g., entering a house) did not occur, so no divorce happened; the wife says it did occur and divorce took place. Recognize this as a conflict over existence of a condition.
2
Determine the default state (asl)
The original state (asl) is that the condition has not occurred. This is based on istishab—the continuation of what was. The husband's statement aligns with this default.
Hanafi usul: 'al-asl baqa' ma kana 'ala ma kana'
3
Classify the parties: claimant vs. defendant
The wife claims something contrary to the default (divorce occurred), making her the claimant (mudda'i). The husband denies the change, making him the defendant (mudda'a alayh). In Hanafi procedure, the burden of proof is on the claimant.
If no evidence, the defendant's word is accepted (with an oath, though here oath is not mentioned for this private matter).
4
Apply the evidentiary rule
Since the wife has no witnesses (bayyinah), the husband's word prevails. If she brings acceptable evidence, that evidence overrides the default, and divorce is established.
The hadith cited: 'If the claimant has no proof, the defendant's word is taken.'
5
Appreciate the second proof
The text adds that the husband denies both the divorce and the loss of ownership (zawal al-milk). The wife claims both. As a denier, the husband's word is given credence in the absence of proof.
Double denial strengthens his position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و ان اختلفا في الشرط فالقول قول الزوج الا ان تقيم المرأة البيئة لانه متمسك بالاصل وهو عدم الشرط ولانه منكر وقوع الطلاق وزوال الملك والمرأة تدعيه
ترجمہ اور اگر دونوں (میاں بیوی) نے شرط میں اختلاف کیا تو شوہر کا قول ( معتبر ہوگا ) مگر یہ کہ عورت گواہ قائم کر دے کیونکہ شوہر اصل سے دلیل پکڑنے والا ہے اور وہ عدم شرط ہے اور اسلئے کہ شوہر وقوع طلاق اور زوال ملک کا منکر ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر اور اس کی بیوی نے وجود شرط میں اختلاف کیا مثلاً شوہر کہتا ہے کہ شرط نہیں پائی گئی اور نہ طلاق واقع ہوئی۔ اور عورت کہتی ہے کہ شرط پائی گئی اور طلاق واقع ہوگئی۔ تو اس صورت میں اگر عورت کے پاس گواہ موجود نہ ہوں تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اگر عورت کے پاس گواہ موجود ہیں تو ان کی گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کا قول اصل کے موافق ہے کیونکہ اصل عدم شرط ہے اور جس کا قول اصل کے موافق ہو وہ مدعی علیہ کہلاتا ہے۔ پس عورت مدعیہ اور شوہر مدعی علیہ ہوا۔ اور حدیث میں ہے کہ اگر مدعی کے پاس بینہ موجود نہ وہ تو مدعلی علیہ کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر وقوع طلاق اور زوال ملک کا منکر ہے اور عورت ان دونوں چیزوں کی مدعیہ ہے اور گواہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں منکر کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس مسئلہ میں اگر عورت کے پاس بینہ موجود نہ ہوتو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
And if they (the spouses) differ about the condition, then the word is the word of the husband, unless the wife establishes proof (bayyinah) because he adheres to the original state (al-asl), which is non-occurrence of the condition, and because he denies the occurrence of divorce and loss of ownership, while the wife claims it. Translation: And if the two (husband and wife) differ about the condition, the husband's word is (believed) except if the wife produces witnesses, because the husband holds onto the original state, which is non-occurrence of the condition, and because the husband denies the occurrence of divorce and loss of ownership, while the wife claims it. Commentary: The situation is that if the husband and his wife differ about the occurrence of the condition—e.g., the husband says the condition did not occur and no divorce took place, and the wife says the condition occurred and divorce took place—then in this case, if the wife has no witnesses, the husband's word is believed. If the wife has witnesses, their testimony will be accepted. The proof is that the husband's word agrees with the original state because the original is non-occurrence of the condition; one whose word agrees with the original is called the defendant (mudda'a alayh). So the wife is the claimant and the husband is the defendant. And in the hadith: 'If the claimant does not have proof, then the word of the defendant is believed.' The second proof is that the husband denies the occurrence of divorce and loss of ownership, and the wife claims these two things; in the absence of witnesses, the word of the denier is believed. For this reason, in this issue, if the wife does not have proof, the husband's word will be believed.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding disputes between spouses over whether the condition of a conditional divorce occurred. The rule: the husband's word is taken as true, unless the wife brings legal evidence (bayyinah). The commentator explains the reasoning: the original state (asl) is that the condition has not occurred (istishab al-hal). The husband's assertion matches this default, making him the defendant (mudda'a alayh) and the wife the claimant. In Islamic legal procedure, the burden of proof is on the claimant; if the claimant has no evidence, the defendant's sworn denial is accepted. A hadith is cited: 'If the claimant has no proof, then the oath is on the defendant.' Here, instead of an oath, the husband's bare word is accepted because the matter is about a private marital affair. Additionally, the husband is denying two things: occurrence of divorce and loss of ownership (that would follow from the divorce). The wife is claiming both. Since the husband is the denier, his word is preferred in the absence of proof. This principle applies when the condition is something potentially observable, like entering a house.

Key Terms
بینہ (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females in financial matters, but here it refers to any proof of the condition's occurrence.
اصل (asl): The original state or default presumption, here the non-occurrence of the condition (istishab).
مدعی (mudda'i): The claimant, the one who asserts something contrary to the default (here the wife).
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a alayh): The defendant, the one whose statement aligns with the asl (here the husband).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband claims the condition (entering a house) did not occur; the wife claims it did. She has no witnesses. What is the ruling?
A) The wife's word is accepted because she is the subject of the divorce.
B) The husband's word is accepted because the original state is non-occurrence.
C) Both must take an oath.
D) The judge decides based on their demeanor.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over conditional divorce, the husband's word is taken as true due to the default presumption of non-occurrence, unless the wife brings acceptable evidence.

Condition Known Only to Wife: Her Word Accepted for Herself
Ruling with proof: istihsan overriding qiyas in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to determine when a wife's word is accepted in conditional divorce and distinguish cases affecting only herself from those affecting a co-wife.

Core Idea
In matters known only to her, the wife is trustworthy; her word binds herself but not others.

The Hanafi school often uses istihsan to override strict analogy (qiyas) when necessity demands. A classic example is the conditional divorce where the condition—such as menstruation—can only be known by the wife. This lesson walks through the legal reasoning that accepts her word for herself but not against a co-wife, highlighting the delicate balance between private knowledge and evidentiary fairness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition type
Determine whether the condition in the divorce is something that can only be known by the wife (e.g., menstruation) or could be verified externally (e.g., entering a house).
2
Apply qiyas reasoning
By qiyas, the wife would not be believed because conditions require external proof; compare to the case of entering a house where her word alone is insufficient.
3
Apply istihsan reasoning
Istihsan accepts her word because she is the sole source of knowledge, analogous to 'iddah and ghashyan. This prevents hardship.
4
Distinguish personal vs. third-party effect
Her word is accepted for herself but not for a co-wife, because she is a witness against a rival and is suspected of bias (muttahamah).
5
Extract the thamarah
The practical result: if she claims the condition occurred, she alone is divorced; the co-wife is not affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كان الشرط لا يعلم الامن جهتها فالقول قولها في حق نفسها مثل ان يقول ان حضت فانت طالق وفلانة فقالت قدحضت طلقت هي ولم تطلق فلانة ووقوع الطلاق استحسان والقياس ان لا يقع لانه شرط فلا تصدق كما فى الدخول وجه الاستحسان انها امينة في حق نفسها اذ لا يعلم ذلك الامن جهتها فيقبل قولها كما قيل في حق العدة والغشيان ولكنها شاهدة فى حق ضرتهابل هي متهمة فلا يقبل قولها في حقها ترجمہ پھر اگر شرط ( ایسی چیز ہے) جو معلوم نہیں ہو سکتی مگر عورت کی جانب سے تو عورت کا قول اس کی ذلت کے حق میں ( معتبر ہوگا ) مثلاً یہ کہے اگر تو حائضہ ہوئی تو ، تو اور فلاں (عورت) طالقہ ہیں اس نے کہا میں حائضہ ہو گئی تو یہ خود طالقہ ہوگئی اور فلانہ عورت طالقہ نہ ہو گی۔ اور وقوع طلاق استحسان ہے اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ واقع نہ ہو کیونکہ یہ شرط ہے تو عورت کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ جیسا کہ ( دخول دار ) کی صورت میں ۔ اور استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ عورت اپنی ذات کے حق میں امانت دار ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بات سوائے اس کے دوسری جہت سے معلوم نہیں ہو سکتی ، لہذا عورت ہی کا قول قبول ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ عدت اور ولی کے حق میں کہا گیا ہے۔ اور لیکن یہ عورت اپنی سوتن کے حق میں گواہ ہے بلکہ مہتمہ ہے۔ لہذا اس کا قول اس کی سوتن کے حق میں قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شرط ایسی چیز ہے جس کا علم صرف عورت کو ہوسکتا ہے۔ دوسروں کونہیں ہوسکتا تو وجود شرط میں اس کا
And if the condition is not known except from her side, then the word is her word regarding herself. For example, he says, 'If you menstruate, then you and so-and-so (a co-wife) are divorced.' She says, 'I have menstruated,' then she is divorced, and so-and-so is not divorced. And the occurrence of divorce is istihsan; by qiyas, it would not occur because it is a condition, so she is not to be believed, as in the case of entering a house. The face of istihsan: she is trustworthy regarding herself because that matter is not known except from her, so her statement is accepted, as said regarding 'iddah and ghashyan (covering). But she is a witness regarding her co-wife; rather, she is suspect (muttahamah), so her statement regarding her (co-wife) is not accepted. Translation: Then if the condition is something that cannot be known except from the woman's side, then the woman's word is accepted regarding herself. For example, he says, 'If you menstruate, then you and so-and-so (woman) are divorced.' She says, 'I have menstruated,' then she herself is divorced, and so-and-so woman is not divorced. And the occurrence of divorce is istihsan; by qiyas it would not occur because it is a condition, so she is not to be believed, as in the case of entering a house. The evidence for istihsan: this woman is trustworthy regarding herself because this matter cannot be known except from her, so her statement is accepted, as said regarding 'iddah and ghashyan. But she is a witness regarding her co-wife; rather, she is suspect, so her statement regarding her co-wife is not accepted. Commentary: The situation is that if the condition is something that only the wife can know about, such as the start of menstruation, then her claim that it occurred is accepted only for herself. She cannot extend that claim to affect a co-wife because she would be a witness in that matter and is also suspected of bias.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that involves an intra-Hanafi dispute between qiyas and istihsan. The issue: when the condition of a conditional divorce is something only the wife can know (e.g., her own menstruation), is her word accepted? By strict qiyas (analogy), she would not be believed because the condition is a factual event that could theoretically be verified by others, and allowing her to self-report would be like the case of entering a house where her word is not accepted alone. However, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference): for matters that are inherently private and cannot be verified by others, the woman is considered trustworthy (aminah) regarding herself. This is analogous to the rules of 'iddah (waiting period) where the woman's report of her own menstrual cycle is accepted, and the rule of ghashyan (covering) in prayer. Therefore, her word is accepted for herself. But when a co-wife is involved, the woman becomes a witness against a third party and is also suspected (muttahamah) of bias, so her statement does not affect the co-wife. Thus, if a husband says to two wives, 'If you (both) menstruate' or 'If you (one wife) menstruate, both are divorced,' only the one who reports menstruation is divorced; the other is not affected. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of distinguishing between personal rights (where one's own testimony is accepted in private matters) and third-party rights (where impartial witnesses are needed).

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas (analogy) in favor of equity and practicality; here, accepting the wife's word despite the general rule against self-testimony.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that would reject the wife's claim by comparing to cases like entering a house.
امین (amin): Trustworthy; the wife is deemed trustworthy regarding her own private conditions.
سوتن (sotan): Co-wife (darrat); the wife's statement does not affect her co-wife due to partiality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his two wives, 'If you menstruate, both of you are divorced.' The first wife says she menstruated; the second says nothing. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Both are divorced because the condition is general.
B) Only the first wife is divorced; the second is not.
C) Neither is divorced because the husband must verify.
D) The second wife is divorced because the first's claim implicates her.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, for conditions known only to the wife, her word is accepted for herself by istihsan, but it does not bind a co-wife due to potential bias.

Whose Word is Accepted in a Dispute Over a Condition in Suspended Divorce
Ruling on evidence in a conditional divorce dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whose word is accepted when a husband and wife dispute the occurrence of a condition in suspended divorce, and explain the two proofs (dalil) for this ruling.

Core Idea
In a dispute about a suspended divorce condition, the husband's word prevails unless the wife brings evidence—the denier's oath wins.

In Islamic family law, suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) is conditional. If the husband and wife disagree on whether the condition occurred, who is trusted? The Hanafi school has a clear rule: the husband's word is taken unless the wife has evidence. This lesson examines the legal basis for this ruling, rooted in the principle that the original state is absence, and the burden of proof is on the claimant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exception
Read the passage closely. What is the default ruling? Under what condition does the wife's word become accepted?
The exception is evidence (bayyinah).
2
Understand the first proof: original state
The husband's word aligns with the original state (asl) that the condition did not occur. Explain why this makes him the defendant (mudda‘a alayh).
The principle: 'al-asl baqa' ma kana 'ala ma kana' — the original state remains.
3
Understand the second proof: denier status
The husband denies the divorce and loss of ownership, making him the denier (munkir). The wife is the claimant (mudda‘iyah). State the general hadith principle that applies.
Hadith: 'If the claimant has no evidence, the denier's statement is taken.'
4
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Given a scenario where the wife has two witnesses, how does the ruling change? Describe the legal effect.
The wife's evidence shifts the burden, and her claim is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر شرط میں زوجین کا اختلاف ہو جائے تو کس کا قول معتبر ہے
و ان اختلفا في الشرط فالقول قول الزوج الا ان تقيم المرأة البينة لانه متمسك بالاصل وهو عدم الشرط ولانه منكر وقوع الطلاق وزوال الملك والمرأة تدعيه
ترجمہ اور اگر دونوں (میاں بیوی) نے شرط میں اختلاف کیا تو شوہر کا قول ( معتبر ہوگا ) مگر یہ کہ عورت گواہ قائم کر دے کیونکہ شوہر اصل سے دلیل پکڑنے والا ہے اور وہ عدم شرط ہے اور اسلئے کہ شوہر وقوع طلاق اور زوال ملک کا منکر ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر اور اس کی بیوی نے وجود شرط میں اختلاف کیا مثلاً شوہر کہتا ہے کہ شرط نہیں پائی گئی اور نہ طلاق واقع ہوئی۔ اور عورت کہتی ہے کہ شرط پائی گئی اور طلاق واقع ہوگئی۔ تو اس صورت میں اگر عورت کے پاس گواہ موجود نہ ہوں تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ اور اگر عورت کے پاس گواہ موجود ہیں تو ان کی گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کا قول اصل کے موافق ہے کیونکہ اصل عدم شرط ہے اور جس کا قول اصل کے موافق ہو وہ مدعی علیہ کہلاتا ہے۔ پس عورت مدعیہ اور شوہر مدعی علیہ ہوا۔ اور حدیث میں ہے کہ اگر مدعی کے پاس بینہ موجود نہ وہ تو مدعلی علیہ کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر وقوع طلاق اور زوال ملک کا منکر ہے اور عورت ان دونوں چیزوں کی مدعیہ ہے اور گواہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں منکر کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس مسئلہ میں اگر عورت کے پاس بینہ موجود نہ ہوتو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔
If the husband and wife dispute over the condition, then the word is the word of the husband unless the woman presents evidence, because he is adhering to the original state, which is the absence of the condition, and because he is denying the occurrence of divorce and the removal of ownership, while the woman claims it.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on whose statement is accepted when a husband and wife disagree about whether a condition for a suspended divorce occurred. The ruling: the husband's word is taken, unless the wife provides clear evidence (bayyinah). This is because the husband is the one who originally is free from the condition (original state is absence), so he is the defendant (mudda'a alayh) and the wife is the claimant (mudda'iyah). The general legal principle from hadith is that the burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the denier. Therefore, without evidence, the husband's denial prevails. The text provides two proofs: (1) the husband holds the original state of no condition, (2) the husband is denying divorce and loss of ownership, so he is the denier, and the denier's word is accepted.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition upon which divorce is suspended, e.g., 'if you enter the house, you are divorced'.
بينة (bayyinah): Clear evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females, to prove the occurrence of the condition.
مدعی (mudda'i): The claimant who asserts the occurrence of the condition and divorce; the wife.
منکر (munkir): The denier who rejects the claim; the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute about whether a condition for a suspended divorce occurred, whose word is accepted if the wife has no witnesses?
A) The wife's word
B) The husband's word
C) The qadi's decision
D) The witnesses from the community

Key Takeaway
The husband's word is accepted in disputed conditions for suspended divorce unless the wife provides evidence, based on the principle that the denier's statement stands when the claimant lacks proof.

Talaq — Divorce

Condition Known Only by Wife: Her Word Accepted for Herself but Not Co-Wife
Ruling on wife's statement when condition is only knowable by her, with istihsan vs qiyas analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a divorce condition is only knowable by the wife and explain why her statement is accepted for herself but not for her co-wife.

Core Idea
Her word is accepted for herself but not for her co-wife—trustworthiness ends where bias begins.

This lesson tackles a nuanced case in suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). When the husband makes divorce conditional on a matter only the wife can know, such as her menstruation, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to accept her word for herself, but not against her co-wife. We will explore the underlying logic, the Quranic proof, and the distinction between qiyas and istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the scenario: husband says 'If you menstruate, you and so-and-so (co-wife) are divorced.' The wife claims menstruation. The Hanafi ruling: she is divorced, but the co-wife is not divorced.
2
Understand the two legal methods
Qiyas would reject her claim entirely because she is a claimant without evidence. Istihsan overrides qiyas and accepts her word for herself.
The author states: 'ووقوع الطلاق استحسان والقياس ان لا يقع'.
3
Examine the basis for istihsan
The wife is considered trustworthy (amin) regarding matters only she can know, like menstruation. The Quran (2:228) commands women not to conceal what is in their wombs, supporting her trustworthiness.
Dalil: لا يحل لهن ان يكتمن ما خلق الله في ارحامهن
4
Note the limitation for the co-wife
She is not believed regarding the co-wife because she is a witness with potential bias (mutahhamah). Her word is not accepted against another party.
The author says: 'لكنها شاهدة فى حق ضرتها بل هي متهمة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر شرط ایسی ہے کہ عورت ہی سے معلوم ہو سکتی ہے تو عورت کا قول اس کے حق میں معتبر ہوگا
فان كان الشرط لا يعلم الامن جهتها فالقول قولها في حق نفسها مثل ان يقول ان حضت فانت طالق وفلانة فقالت قدحضت طلقت هي ولم تطلق فلانة ووقوع الطلاق استحسان والقياس ان لا يقع لانه شرط فلا تصدق كما فى الدخول وجه الاستحسان انها امينة في حق نفسها اذ لا يعلم ذلك الامن جهتها فيقبل قولها كما قيل في حق العدة والغشيان ولكنها شاهدة فى حق ضرتهابل هي متهمة فلا يقبل قولها في حقها
ترجمہ پھر اگر شرط ( ایسی چیز ہے) جو معلوم نہیں ہو سکتی مگر عورت کی جانب سے تو عورت کا قول اس کی ذات کے حق میں ( معتبر ہوگا ) مثلاً یہ کہے اگر تو حائضہ ہوئی تو ، تو اور فلاں (عورت) طالقہ ہیں اس نے کہا میں حائضہ ہو گئی تو یہ خود طالقہ ہوگئی اور فلانہ عورت طالقہ نہ ہو گی۔ اور وقوع طلاق استحسان ہے اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ واقع نہ ہو کیونکہ یہ شرط ہے تو عورت کی تصدیق نہ ہوگی۔ جیسا کہ ( دخول دار ) کی صورت میں ۔ اور استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ عورت اپنی ذات کے حق میں امانت دار ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ بات سوائے اس کے دوسری جہت سے معلوم نہیں ہو سکتی ، لہذا عورت ہی کا قول قبول ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ عدت اور وطی کے حق میں کہا گیا ہے۔ اور لیکن یہ عورت اپنی سوتن کے حق میں گواہ ہے بلکہ مہتمہ ہے۔ لہذا اس کا قول اس کی سوتن کے حق میں قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شرط ایسی چیز ہے جس کا علم صرف عورت کو ہوسکتا ہے۔ دوسروں کونہیں ہوسکتا تو وجود شرط میں اس کا قول صرف اس کی ذات کے حق میں قبول ہوگا دوسرے کے حق میں قبول نہیں ہوگا۔ یہی قول ہے امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ مثلاً شوہر نے اپنی ایک بیوی سے کہا ان حضت فانت طالق و فلانة (فلانہ سے اس کی دوسری بیوی مراد ہے)۔ اس عورت نے کہا مجھے حیض آگیا تو یہ مطلقہ ہوگئی۔ اور فلانہ یعنی اس کی سوتن کو طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی۔ یہ بات یادر ہے کہ اس کی سوتن کو طلاق کا واقع نہ ہونا اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ شوہر نے اس کے قول حضت میں اسکی تکذیب کی ہو ورنہ اگر شوہر نے اس کی تصدیق کر دی تو دونوں کو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔
اس مسئلہ میں طلاق کا واقع ہونا استحسانا ہے اور قیاس کا مقتضیٰ یہ ہے کہ طلاق واقع نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ ان حضت فانت طالق میں حیض شرط ہے۔ اور عورت اس وجود شرط کی مدعیہ ہے۔ اور شوہر منکر ۔ اور بینہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں منکر کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا یہاں کے گی۔ جیسا دار پایا اور نے انکار دیا کے کی نہیں عورت کے قول کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ جیسا کہ اگر دخول دار پایا گیا اور شوہر نے انکار کر دیا تو عورت کے قول کی تصدیق نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت اپنی ذات کے حق میں امانت دار ہے۔ کیونکہ عورتیں مافی الارحام کو ظاہر کرنے میں امانت دار بھی ہیں اور مامور بھی ہیں۔ خداوند قدوس کا ارشاد ہے لا يحل لهن ان يكتمن ما خلق الله في ارحامهن ۔ اور اس وجہ سے بھی عورت امانت دار ہے کہ حیض ایسی شرط ہے جس کا علم صرف اس کو ہو سکتا ہے اس کے علاوہ کو نہیں ہوسکتا۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ امین کا قول اس کے حق میں قابل قبول ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے عورت کا قول ( کہ مجھ کو حیض آگیا) اس کے حق میں قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ عدت اور وطی کے حق میں عورت کا قول قبول کیا جائے گا۔ عدت کے حق میں قبول کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عورت کہے کہ میری عدت پوری ہوگئی یا پوری نہیں ہوئی۔ اس میں عورت ہی کا قول معتبر ہو گا نہ کہ مرد کا۔ اور وطی کے حق میں قبول ہونے کے دو مطلب ہو سکے ہیں ایک یہ کہ مطلقہ ثلث کہے کہ میری عدت پوری ہو گئی اور میں نے زوج آخر سے نکاح کیا اور زوج ثانی میرے ساتھ دخول بھی کر چکا تو اس زوج ثانی کے دخول کرنے میں عورت کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ جماع کرنا چاہتا ہے تو بیوی کے پاک یا حائضہ ہونے میں عورت ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ البتہ یہ عورت اپنی سوتن پر طلاق واقع ہونے کے سلسلہ میں شاہدہ ہے بلکہ مہم ہے کیونکہ کبھی انسان یہ چاہتا ہے کہ میں رہوں یا نہ رہوں لیکن میرا حریف نہ رہے۔ پس یہاں بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس عورت کے دل میں یہی جذبہ کار فرما رہا ہو کہ میں بیوی بن کر رہوں یا نہ رہوں لیکن میری سوتن نہ رہنی چاہئے ، اس موقع کیلئے کہا گیا ہے
ہم تو ڈوبے ہیں صنم تم کو بھی لے ڈوبیں گے
خلاصہ یہ کہ یہ عورت اپنی سوتن کے حق میں متہمہ ہے اور متہمہ کی شہادت مردود ہوتی ہے اسلئے اس عورت کا قول ( کہ مجھے حیض آگیا )
اس کی سوتن کے حق میں قابل قبول نہ ہوگا۔
If the condition is only known from her side, then the word is her word regarding herself, such as if he says: 'If you menstruate, you and so-and-so are divorced,' and she says, 'I have menstruated,' she is divorced and so-and-so is not divorced. The occurrence of divorce is istihsan, and qiyas is that it does not occur because it is a condition, so she is not believed, as in the case of entry. The basis of istihsan is that she is trustworthy regarding herself, since that is not known except from her side, so her word is accepted, as said regarding 'iddah and coitus. But she is a witness regarding her co-wife; rather she is accused, so her word is not accepted regarding her.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific scenario where the condition for a suspended divorce is something only the wife can know, such as her own menstruation. The ruling: if the husband says 'If you menstruate, you and my other wife are divorced,' and the wife claims menstruation, then by istihsan (juristic preference) she is divorced herself, but the co-wife is not divorced. Qiyas (analogy) would say that her word is not accepted at all because she is a claimant and the husband is the denier, similar to the case of entering a house where the claim is not accepted. However, istihsan overrides because the wife is trustworthy (amin) regarding her own body, and the Quran commands women not to conceal what is in their wombs (Quran 2:228). Therefore, her statement is accepted for herself. But she is not trustworthy regarding her co-wife; she is an accused witness (mutahhamah) because she may have a motive to harm her rival, so her word is not accepted against the co-wife unless the husband confirms it. The passage also draws analogies to 'iddah (waiting period) and intercourse where the wife's word is accepted on matters only she can know.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a ruling that better serves justice, here because the wife is trustworthy.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that would reject the wife's claim because she is a claimant without evidence.
امین (amin): Trustworthy; the wife is considered trustworthy regarding matters only she can know, such as her own menstruation.
متہمہ (mutahhamah): Accused; the wife is considered potentially biased against her co-wife, so her testimony is not accepted against her.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife: 'If you menstruate, you and my other wife are divorced,' and the wife claims menstruation, what is the ruling?
A) Both are divorced
B) Neither is divorced
C) The wife is divorced, but the co-wife is not
D) The wife is not divorced, but the co-wife is

Key Takeaway
In ta'liq al-talaq, when the condition is only known to the wife, her statement is accepted for herself by istihsan, but not against a co-wife due to potential bias.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Woman's Statement on Menstruation: Istihsan over Qiyas
Ruling with proof on accepting woman's menstruation claim for herself only

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a woman's statement about her own menstruation is accepted (by istihsan) in conditional divorce, and distinguish this from when her statement affects others.

Core Idea
A woman is trusted about her own menstruation but not about her co-wife's divorce.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband makes divorce conditional on menstruation, only the woman knows if the condition occurred. Should her statement be accepted? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling that, by istihsan, her word is taken for herself but not for her co-wife, supported by the Quranic trust in women about their bodies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the example
Read the example: a husband says to his wife 'If you menstruate, you are divorced and so is my other wife.' The woman claims menstruation. What is the ruling?
The ruling: she is divorced but the co-wife is not, unless the husband confirms.
2
Understand the qiyas argument
Qiyas would suggest the woman's statement should not be accepted because she is the claimant and the husband is the denier; the denier's statement is normally accepted.
General principle: in absence of evidence, the denier's statement prevails.
3
Analyze the istihsan exception
The Hanafi school overrides qiyas with istihsan based on the woman's trustworthiness (amin) regarding her own body, as supported by Quran 2:228.
The verse prohibits concealing what is in the wombs, indicating women are entrusted with such knowledge.
4
Apply the distinction between self and others
The woman is considered trustworthy for herself, but regarding her co-wife, she is a witness with potential bias (mutahhamah), so her statement is rejected.
This prevents a wife from maliciously triggering divorce for her co-wife.
5
Note the condition of husband's denial
The ruling that the co-wife is not divorced applies only if the husband denies the woman's claim. If he confirms, both are divorced.
The husband's confirmation overrides the rejection of her testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول صرف اس کی ذات کے حق میں قبول ہوگا دوسرے کے حق میں قبول نہیں ہوگا۔ یہی قول ہے امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ مثلاً شوہر نے اپنی ایک بیوی سے کہا ان حضت فانت طالق و فلانة (فلانہ سے اس کی دوسری بیوی مراد ہے)۔ اس عورت نے کہا مجھے حیض آگیا تو یہ مطلقہ ہوگئی۔ اور فلانہ یعنی اس کی سوتن کو طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی۔ یہ بات یادر ہے کہ اس کی سوتن کو طلاق کا واقع نہ ہونا اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ شوہر نے اس کے قول حضت میں اسکی تکذیب کی ہو ورنہ اگر شوہر نے اس کی تصدیق کر دی تو دونوں کو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔
اس مسئلہ میں طلاق کا واقع ہونا استحسانا ہے اور قیاس کا مقتضیٰ یہ ہے کہ طلاق واقع نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ ان حضت فانت طالق میں حیض شرط ہے۔ اور عورت اس وجود شرط کی مدعیہ ہے۔ اور شوہر منکر ۔ اور بینہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں منکر کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا یہاں کے گی۔ جیسا دار پایا اور نے انکار دیا کے کی نہیں عورت کے قول کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ جیسا کہ اگر دخول دار پایا گیا اور شوہر نے انکار کر دیا تو عورت کے قول کی تصدیق نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت اپنی ذات کے حق میں امانت دار ہے۔ کیونکہ عورتیں مافی الارحام کو ظاہر کرنے میں امانت دار بھی ہیں اور مامور بھی ہیں۔ خداوند قدوس کا ارشاد ہے لا يحل لهن ان يكتمن ما خلق الله في ارحامهن ۔ اور اس وجہ سے بھی عورت امانت دار ہے کہ حیض ایسی شرط ہے جس کا علم صرف اس کو ہو سکتا ہے اس کے علاوہ کو نہیں ہوسکتا۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ امین کا قول اس کے حق میں قابل قبول ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے عورت کا قول ( کہ مجھ کو حیض آگیا) اس کے حق میں قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ عدت اور وطی کے حق میں عورت کا قول قبول کیا جائے گا۔ عدت کے حق میں قبول کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عورت کہے کہ میری عدت پوری ہوگئی یا پوری نہیں ہوئی۔ اس میں عورت ہی کا قول معتبر ہو گا نہ کہ مرد کا۔ اور وطی کے حق میں قبول ہونے کے دو مطلب ہو سکے ہیں ایک یہ کہ مطلقہ ثلث کہے کہ میری عدت پوری ہو گئی اور میں نے زوج آخر سے نکاح کیا اور زوج ثانی میرے ساتھ دخول بھی کر چکا تو اس زوج ثانی کے دخول کرنے میں عورت کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ جماع کرنا چاہتا ہے تو بیوی کے پاک یا حائضہ ہونے میں عورت ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ البتہ یہ عورت اپنی سوتن پر طلاق واقع ہونے کے سلسلہ میں شاہدہ ہے بلکہ مہم ہے کیونکہ کبھی انسان یہ چاہتا ہے کہ میں رہوں یا نہ رہوں لیکن میرا حریف نہ رہے۔ پس یہاں بھی ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس عورت کے دل میں یہی جذبہ کار فرما رہا ہو کہ میں بیوی بن کر رہوں یا نہ رہوں لیکن میری سوتن نہ رہنی چاہئے ، اس موقع کیلئے کہا گیا ہے ہم تو ڈوبے ہیں صنم تم کو بھی لے ڈوبیں گے خلاصہ یہ کہ یہ عورت اپنی سوتن کے حق میں متہمہ ہے اور متہمہ کی شہادت مردود ہوتی ہے اسلئے اس عورت کا قول ( کہ مجھے حیض آگیا ) اس کی سوتن کے حق میں قابل قبول نہ ہوگا۔
The statement will only be accepted regarding her own self; regarding another, it will not be accepted. This is the saying of Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad. For example, the husband said to one of his wives: 'If you menstruate, then you are divorced, and so-and-so (meaning his other wife).' That woman said, 'I have menstruated,' so she becomes divorced. And so-and-so, i.e., her co-wife, divorce does not occur. It should be remembered that the non-occurrence of divorce to her co-wife is when the husband has belied her statement of menstruation; otherwise, if the husband verified her, then both would be divorced. In this issue, the occurrence of divorce is by istihsan, and the requirement of qiyas is that divorce should not occur. Because in 'If you menstruate, you are divorced,' menstruation is a condition. The woman claims the existence of the condition, and the husband denies it. And in the absence of evidence, the statement of the denier is considered. Therefore, here... like if [something] is found and he denied, the woman's statement is not verified. Just as if intercourse is found and the husband denied, the woman's statement is not verified. And the proof of istihsan is that the woman is trustworthy regarding herself. Because women are trustworthy in revealing what is in the wombs and also commanded. Allah, the Holy, says: 'It is not lawful for them to conceal what Allah has created in their wombs.' And also for this reason the woman is trustworthy: that menstruation is a condition whose knowledge only she can have, no one else. And the rule is that the statement of a trustee is acceptable regarding his own right. For this reason, the woman's statement (that I have menstruated) will be accepted regarding herself. Just as in 'iddah and intercourse, the woman's statement is accepted. The meaning of acceptance for 'iddah is that the woman says her 'iddah is completed or not completed; her statement is considered, not the man's. For intercourse, there are two meanings: first, a thrice-divorced woman says her 'iddah is completed and she married another husband and he consummated, then her statement about the second husband's consummation is accepted. Second, if the husband wants to have intercourse with his wife, the woman's statement regarding whether she is pure or menstruating is accepted. However, this woman, regarding the occurrence of divorce to her co-wife, is a witness, rather a plaintiff, because sometimes a person wants that he remains or not, but his rival does not remain. So here too, it is possible that the same feeling worked in her heart: 'Let me remain a wife or not, but my co-wife should not remain.' For this occasion it is said: 'We have drowned, beloved, we will drown you too.' The conclusion is that this woman is accused regarding her co-wife, and the testimony of an accused is rejected, therefore her statement (that I have menstruated) will not be acceptable regarding her co-wife.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on conditional divorce linked to menstruation and explains the Hanafi position with proofs. The passage begins by stating the ruling: if a husband says to one wife 'If you menstruate, you are divorced and my other wife is also divorced,' and she claims menstruation, she is divorced but the other is not, unless the husband confirms her claim. The text then notes that the same ruling is held by Imams Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad. Next, the passage explains the legal reasoning: qiyas (analogy) would suggest no divorce occurs because the wife claims a condition, the husband denies, and the denier's statement is generally accepted in the absence of evidence. However, the ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), which overrides qiyas. The proof for istihsan is that the woman is considered trusty (amin) regarding herself, supported by the Quranic verse: 'It is not lawful for them to conceal what Allah has created in their wombs' (2:228). The passage also analogizes to other situations where a woman's statement is accepted: 'iddah and intercourse. However, for the co-wife, the woman is not a trustee but a witness with a potential bias, so her statement is not accepted. The commentary concludes by emphasizing that the woman is accused regarding her co-wife, and the testimony of an accused is rejected.

Key Terms
حیض (hayd): Menstruation, used as a condition for conditional divorce in the example.
امانت دار (amanat dar): Trustworthy; the woman is considered trustworthy (amin) regarding her own statements about bodily matters.
متہمہ (mutahhamah): Accused or suspected; the woman is considered accused regarding her co-wife, so her testimony is rejected.
شاہدہ (shahidah): Witness; the woman is considered a witness regarding her co-wife's divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both wives are divorced.
B) Neither wife is divorced.
C) Only the first wife is divorced.
D) The statement is invalid entirely.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a woman's statement about her own menstruation is accepted by istihsan for herself but not for others, preventing both injustice and abuse.

Acceptance of Woman's Claim in Conditional Divorce
Ruling with proof on accepting woman's claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a woman's statement about her own state is accepted for herself but not for others in conditional divorce cases.

Core Idea
A woman's statement about herself is accepted even if improbable, but not for others.

This lesson extends the principle from the previous one: a woman's claim about her own subjective state—like loving hellfire or loving her husband—is accepted as true for herself, because she is the trusted authority on her own feelings. However, for others (like a co-wife or slave), her statement is considered witness testimony and is not accepted due to potential bias. We will examine two cases and the rational proof behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the two conditional divorce scenarios: (1) husband conditions divorce on wife's love of hellfire, (2) conditions on wife's love of him. Note the different outcomes for wife vs. slave/co-wife.
Both involve the wife's claim about her own love.
2
State the ruling per case
For each case, determine the outcome: the wife is divorced if she claims love, but the slave is not freed and the co-wife is not divorced.
Her claim is accepted only for herself.
3
Recognize the principle of amanah (trustworthiness)
The woman is considered amin (trustworthy) regarding her own state, and shahidah (witness) regarding others. A trustee's statement is valid for himself, a witness's is not accepted due to possible interest.
This is the key legal distinction.
4
Analyze the objection and rebuttal
An objector argues that loving hellfire is impossible, so her claim must be a lie. The rebuttal: lying is not certain—she might genuinely prefer hellfire due to extreme hatred or foolishness.
Certainty of falsehood is required to reject her statement.
5
Apply the rule to similar cases
Consider how this principle applies to any conditional divorce involving a subjective state of the wife. The rule is consistent: her word is taken for herself.
This is a manifestation of the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) but here it's about accepting her claim of intention.

The husband said: 'If you love that Allah punish you in the hellfire, then you are divorced and my slave is free.' The woman said: 'I love it.' Then this statement is valid regarding the woman and not regarding the slave. Similarly, the husband said: 'If you love me, then you are divorced and this one (co-wife) is with you.' The woman said: 'I love you.' Then divorce occurs for her and the slave is not freed and her co-wife is not divorced. For the reason we have stated, and there is no certainty of her lying, because due to intense hatred of him, she may love to be relieved by punishment. And regarding herself, the ruling is attached to her report even if she is lying. So regarding others, the ruling remains on the original principle, which is love. Explanation: Two issues are stated: First, the husband says 'If you love that Allah punish you in hellfire, you are divorced and my slave is free.' She says 'I love it,' so her statement is accepted for herself and divorce occurs, but not for the slave. Second, the husband says 'If you love me, you are divorced and this co-wife is with you.' She says 'I love you,' so she is divorced but the co-wife is not. The proof has passed in the first issue: this woman is trustworthy regarding herself and a witness regarding her co-wife and the slave, and the statement of a trustee is only valid for himself, not for others. 'Wa la yunan' (و لا ينان) is an answer to an objection: The objection is that the woman's statement is accepted for herself because she is truthful, but her report about loving hellfire is definitely a lie, since a Muslim loving hellfire is irrational; therefore her statement should not be accepted. The answer is that we are not certain of her lying, because a woman is deficient in intellect and ignorant, and sometimes due to severe oppression from her husband, she might actually prefer hellfire to get rid of him. So her lying is not certain, and therefore her statement is accepted for herself.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents two analogous cases to the previous lesson. In the first case, a husband conditionalizes divorce and freeing a slave on the wife's love of hellfire. She claims she loves hellfire; her claim is accepted for her own divorce but not for freeing the slave. In the second case, the condition is her love for her husband, and her claim results in her divorce but not the co-wife's. The commentary explains that the same principle applies: the woman is trustworthy (amin) regarding herself but a witness (shahidah) regarding others, and her testimony is not accepted due to potential bias. An objection is raised: since no Muslim would truly love hellfire, her claim must be a lie, so it should be rejected entirely. The reply is that her lying is not certain; due to stupidity or severe hatred, she might genuinely prefer hellfire to stay with the husband. Therefore, her statement is accepted for herself, as the ruling is based on her report, not on objective truth. The passage reinforces the Hanafi principle that a person's statement about their own state is accepted, even if improbable, as long as lying is not absolutely certain.

Key Terms
محبت (muhabbat): Love; used as a condition for divorce.
عذاب (adhab): Punishment; specifically hellfire in this context.
صادق (sadiq): Truthful; the assumption that the woman is truthful in her claim about her own state.
کاذبہ (kadhibah): Liar; the objection that the woman must be lying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The condition only applies to divorce, not to freeing the slave.
D) The husband trusts her more for her own affairs.

Key Takeaway
A person's claim about their own internal state is accepted for themselves, even if improbable, as long as there is no certainty of lying.

Talaq — Divorce

Conditional Divorce on Wife's Statement About Love
Explains rulings and reasoning for conditional divorce based on wife's declaration about love

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for conditional divorce when the wife's statement about her internal state is involved, and explain the distinction between her being ameen for herself and shahid for others.

Core Idea
A wife's statement about her own love is accepted for herself but not for co-wife or slave.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses ta'liq al-talaq where the condition depends on the wife's internal feeling of love. It introduces two scenarios: the husband conditions divorce on the wife loving Hellfire punishment or loving him. The key ruling is that the wife's word is taken for herself (since she is ameen regarding her internal state) but not for others (she is a mere shahid). The text also answers an objection about the impossibility of a Muslim truly loving Hellfire.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) Husband says: 'If you love that Allah punish you in Hell, you are divorced and my slave is free.' Wife says: 'I love it.' (2) Husband says: 'If you love me, you are divorced and your co-wife is also divorced.' Wife says: 'I love you.' Note the different outcomes.
In both cases, the condition is about the wife's internal state of love.
2
State the Ruling for the Wife vs Others
In the first case, the wife is divorced but the slave is not freed. In the second, the addressed wife is divorced but the co-wife is not. The principle: her statement is accepted for herself but not for others.
This is the core legal outcome to remember.
3
Understand the Principle: Ameen vs Shahid
The wife is considered ameen (trustworthy) for her own internal state because only she knows it. Therefore her word is accepted for herself. For others (co-wife, slave), she is a shahid (witness) and a single witness without corroboration is insufficient to establish a right for them.
This distinction is rooted in Hanafi rules of evidence and testimony.
4
Analyze the Objection and Its Answer
An objection is raised: How can a Muslim woman truly love Hellfire? She must be lying. The answer: due to weak intellect and possible severe oppression, she might genuinely prefer Hellfire to escape. Thus her lying is not certain, and her statement is accepted for herself even if it might be false.
This shows that the ruling is based on practical possibility, not mere probability.

In her case, the ruling is tied to her report even if she is lying. In the case of others, the ruling remains on the original, which is love. Explanation: Two issues are explained in the text. First: The husband said to his wife: 'If you love that Allah should punish you in Hellfire, then you are divorced and my slave is free,' i.e., he made the divorce of his wife and the freeing of his slave conditional on loving the punishment of Hell. Then the woman said: 'I love the punishment of Hell.' So this statement of hers is accepted for herself, and divorce occurs. However, it is not accepted regarding the slave, and the slave is not freed. Second: The husband said: 'If you love me, then you are divorced, and this one with you.' The woman said: 'I love you.' So in this case, the addressed woman is divorced, not her co-wife. The proof has passed in the first issue that this woman is trustworthy (ameen) for herself, and for her co-wife and the slave she is a witness (shahidah). The statement of the trustworthy is only accepted for her own right, not for others. 'Wa la yuqin' (and it is not certain) is the answer to an objection. The objection is: The woman's statement is accepted for her own right because she is truthful in her statement. But regarding loving the punishment of Hellfire, her report is definitely a lie because a Muslim loving the punishment of Hellfire is contrary to reason. In any case, when we are certain that this woman is lying, her statement should not be accepted at all. The answer is that we cannot be certain that she is lying because women are deficient in intellect and are ignorant. Moreover, sometimes due to the husband's oppression and tyranny, the woman may love the punishment of Hell to get rid of that wicked husband. Therefore, her lying is not certain. When her lying is not certain, the ruling regarding her is tied to her statement even if her statement is false. Regarding others, the ruling remains on the original, which is love, i.e., loving the punishment of Hell or love cannot be known by any proof, so it is not established for others.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage deals with two examples of conditional divorce (ta'liq) where the condition depends on the wife's internal state (love). In both cases, the husband makes a statement that if the wife loves something (punishment or him), she is divorced and/or a slave is freed. The ruling: her word is accepted for herself but not for others. The commentary explains the underlying principle: the wife is ameen (trustworthy) for her own matters because she has exclusive knowledge of her internal state, but she is a shahid (witness) regarding others (co-wife, slave) and a witness's statement alone is not sufficient. An objection is raised: a Muslim woman cannot genuinely love Hellfire, so she must be lying. The answer: due to her weak intellect and possible severe oppression from her husband, she might genuinely prefer even Hellfire as an escape. Thus her truthfulness is not certain, and her statement is accepted for herself. This is a Hanafi application of the principle that a person's word is accepted regarding what only they know, even if it seems improbable.

Key Terms
امین (amīn): Trustworthy; the wife is considered ameen for her own claim about her internal state (love), so her word is accepted for herself.
شاہدہ (shāhidah): Witness; the wife is considered a witness regarding the condition for her co-wife and the slave, meaning her statement is not accepted for them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his wife: 'If you love that Allah should punish you in Hell, then you are divorced and my slave is free.' The wife says: 'I love it.' What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The wife is divorced and the slave is freed.
B) The wife is not divorced and the slave is freed.
C) The wife is divorced and the slave is not freed.
D) Neither the wife is divorced nor the slave is freed.

Key Takeaway
In conditional divorce, a wife's statement about her own internal state (e.g., love) is accepted for herself but not for others, based on the ameen/shahid distinction.

Conditional Divorce on Menstruation: The Three-Day Requirement
Ruling on conditional divorce tied to menstruation with Hanafi three-day minimum hayd requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the minimum hayd is three days to determine the occurrence of a conditional divorce.

Core Idea
A conditional divorce tied to menstruation only takes effect when bleeding lasts at least three days — the Hanafi minimum for hayd.

This lesson examines a conditional divorce (ta'liq) where the husband says 'When you menstruate, you are divorced.' The Hanafi school requires that the bleeding continue for three full days before the condition is considered fulfilled. This ruling is based on the school's definition of the minimum duration of hayd. Understanding this ruling clarifies how timing and continuity affect the validity of conditions in divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional statement and the condition.
The husband says 'When you menstruate, you are divorced.' The condition is the wife becoming menstruating (hā'iḍ).
The statement is a ta'liq (suspensive divorce).
2
Define menstruation (hayḍ) in the Hanafi school.
Hayḍ has a minimum duration of three days and three nights. Bleeding less than that is istiḥāḍah (non-menstrual).
This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the definition to the case.
If bleeding stops before three days, it is not hayḍ; therefore, the condition is not fulfilled and no divorce occurs.
If bleeding continues for three days, the condition is considered fulfilled retroactively from the first sighting.
4
Determine the timing of divorce if condition is fulfilled.
When three days are completed, divorce is ruled to have occurred from the moment bleeding started, because the continuity reveals that it was genuine hayḍ from the beginning.
This affects ʿiddah calculation and other rights.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences.
Other schools (e.g., Shafiʿi) define minimum hayḍ differently (one day), which would change when the condition is deemed satisfied.
This is a legitimate ikhtilāf based on different usūl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر نے کہا اذا حضت فانت طالق عورت نے خون دیکھا طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی یہاں تک کہ تین دن تک خون جاری رہے واذاقال لها اذاحضت فانت طالق فرأت الدم لم يقع الطلاق حتى يستمر ثلثة ايام لان ما ينقطع دونه لا يكون حيضا فاذاتمت ثلثة ايام حكمنا بالطلاق من حين حاضت لانه بالامتداد عرف انه من الرحم فكان حيضا من الابتداء ترجمہ اور جب عورت سے کہا کہ جب تو حائضہ ہو تو ، تو طالقہ ہے پھر اس نے خون دیکھا تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ یہاں تک کہ تین روز تک برابر جاری رہے۔ کیونکہ جو خون تین دن سے کم منقطع ہوتا ہے وہ حیض نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب تین دن پورے ہو گئے تو اس وقت سے وہ حائضہ ہوئی اسی وقت سے طلاق واقع ہونے کا حکم دیں گے۔ کیونکہ تین دن تک ممتد ہونے کی وجہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ خون رحم کا ہے تو وہ شروع ہی سے حیض ہوا۔ تشریح اگر شوہر نے بیوی سے ان حضت فانت طالق کہا پھر اس عورت نے خون دیکھا تو محض خون دیکھنے سے طلاق واقع نہ ہوگی۔ یہاں تک کہ برابر تین دن تک خون جاری رہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک اقل مدت حیض تین دن اور تین راتیں ہیں ۔ اور جو خون اس مدت سے کم میں منقطع ہو جائے گا وہ حیض نہیں ہوگا بلکہ استحاضہ ہوگا۔ البتہ اگر پورے تین دن خون آیا تو جس وقت سے خون آنا شروع ہوا تھا اسی وقت سے طلاق واقع ہونے کا حکم لگا دیا جائے گا کیونکہ تین دن تک خون ممتد ہونے کی وجہ سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ یہ خون رحم کا ہے لہذا اول امر ہی سے حیض شمار ہوگا۔
The husband said: 'When you menstruate, you are divorced.' The woman saw blood. Divorce does not occur until the blood continues for three days. As for when he said to her: 'When you menstruate, you are divorced' and she saw blood, divorce does not fall until it lasts for three days, because that which stops before (three days) is not menstruation. So when three days are completed, we judge that divorce occurred from the time she menstruated, because by its extension it is known that it is from the womb, so it was menstruation from the beginning. Translation: And when a woman is told: 'When you become menstruating, you are divorced,' then she saw blood, divorce does not occur until three full days continue. Because blood that stops less than three days is not hayd. So when three days are completed, she is considered menstruating from that time, and divorce is ruled from that time. Because by extending for three days, it is known that this blood is from the womb, so it was hayd from the start. Explanation: If a husband said to his wife: 'When you menstruate, you are divorced,' then this woman saw blood, merely seeing blood does not cause divorce until blood continues for three full days. The proof is that in our (Hanafi) school, the minimum duration of hayd is three days and three nights. Blood that stops within this duration is not hayd but istihada. However, if three full days of blood occur, then from the moment blood started, divorce is ruled to have occurred because by the extension of blood for three days, it is known that this blood is from the womb, so it is counted as hayd from the beginning.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage addresses a conditional divorce (ta'liq) where the condition is the wife becoming menstruating (ha'id). The Hanafi ruling: divorce does not occur upon merely seeing blood. It only occurs if the blood continues for at least three days (the minimum duration of hayd in the Hanafi school). If the blood stops before three days, it is considered istihada (non-menstrual uterine bleeding) and the condition is not fulfilled. However, if the blood indeed lasts three days, then the divorce is considered to have taken effect from the first sighting of blood, because the continuity reveals that it was genuine hayd from the beginning. This is based on the established Hanafi position that the minimum hayd is three days and three nights. The proof is rational (talil): short bleeding cannot be hayd, so hayd is only confirmed after three days.

Key Terms
حیض (hayḍ): Menstruation; in Hanafi fiqh, the minimum duration is 3 days and 3 nights, maximum 10 days.
استحاضہ (istiḥāḍah): Chronic uterine bleeding that is not menstrual; it occurs when bleeding stops before three days or exceeds ten days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately upon seeing blood.
B) After two days.
C) It does not occur.
D) After three days regardless.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a conditional divorce tied to menstruation requires three continuous days of bleeding to take effect, and if fulfilled, divorce is retroactive to the start of bleeding.

Conditional Divorce on Complete Menstruation: Purification Required
Ruling on conditional divorce tied to complete menstruation (haydah) and the need for tuhur (purification)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on when divorce occurs when the husband uses the wording 'idha hidt haydah' and explain the linguistic proof that the condition requires purification.

Core Idea
A divorce condition tied to 'a haydah' is fulfilled only when menstruation ends with purification, not merely bleeding.

This lesson examines a specific wording in conditional divorce: the husband says 'when you complete a menstruation (haydah), you are divorced.' The Hanafi scholars rule that the divorce does not occur until the wife becomes pure (tahir) after the menstrual bleeding stops. The key lies in the meaning of 'haydah' itself: it denotes a complete menstrual cycle, which is only completed with purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and the ruling
Read the passage and note the condition the husband uses and the ruling: divorce does not occur until the wife becomes pure from that menstruation.
2
Analyze the linguistic proof
The author states that 'haydah' (with the feminine suffix) means a complete menstruation. Examine how this linguistic point supports the ruling.
The completion of hayd is by its termination, which is purification (tuhur).
3
Connect to the hadith of istibra'
The passage references the hadith of istibra', where a woman is required to wait one complete menstruation to verify pregnancy. How does that hadith reinforce the interpretation of 'haydah'?
The hadith uses 'haydah' to mean a full cycle ending with purity.
4
Apply to a scenario
Using the ruling, determine when a wife becomes divorced if she bleeds for several days and then becomes clean.
Divorce occurs only at the point of purification, not at the start or end of bleeding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر شوہر نے کہا اذا حضت حيضة فانت طالق عورت کو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی یہاں تک کہ عورت حیض سے پاک ہو جائے و لو قال لها اذا حضت حيضة فانت طالق لم تطلق حتى تطهر من حيضها لان الحيضة بالهاء هي الكاملة منها و لهذا حمل عليه في حديث الاستبراء وكما لها بانتهائها و ذالك بالطهر ترجمہ اور اگر عورت سے کہا کہ جب تو حائضہ ہو ایک حیض کر کے تو تو طالقہ ہے تو یہ عورت ) طالقہ نہ ہوگی ۔ یہاں تک کہ اس حیض سے پاک ہو جائے کیونکہ حیضتہ باء تاء) کے ساتھ حیض کامل ہے اور اسی وجہ سے حیض کامل پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ حدیث استبراء میں ۔ اور حیض کا کمال اس کی انتہا سے ہوتا ہے اور انتہا طہر سے ہوگی ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا اذا حضت حيضة فانتِ طالق تو یہ عورت مطلقہ نہ ہوگی ۔ یہاں تک کہ اپنے اس حیض سے پاک ہو جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حیضہ بالتا حیض کامل کو کہتے ہیں۔ اور حیض کا کمال اس کے ختم ہونے سے ہوگا اور ختم
If the husband said: 'When you complete a menstruation (haydah), you are divorced,' the woman does not become divorced until she becomes pure from her menstruation. And if he said to her: 'When you complete a menstruation (haydah), you are divorced,' she is not divorced until she becomes clean from her hayd, because 'haydah' with 'hā' (the feminine suffix) is the complete one. For this reason it is interpreted as complete in the hadith of istibrā'. And its completion is by its termination, and that is by purification (ṭuhr). Translation: And if a woman is told: 'When you become menstruating, having one complete menstruation, then you are divorced,' this woman does not become divorced until she becomes clean from that hayd. Because 'hayḍah' with 'tā' is complete hayd, and for this reason it is interpreted as complete hayd in the hadith of istibrā'. And the completion of hayd is by its termination, and termination is by purification. Explanation: The issue is that if a man said to his wife: 'When you complete a menstruation (haydah), you are divorced,' this woman does not become divorced until she becomes pure from that hayd. The proof is that 'hayḍah' with tā indicates complete hayd. And completion of hayd is by its end, and end is by purification.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage deals with a different wording of the condition: instead of 'idhā ḥiḍt' (when you menstruate), the husband says 'idhā ḥiḍt ḥayḍah' (when you complete a menstruation). The Hanafi ruling: divorce does not occur until the wife has completed the menstruation and become pure (ṭāhir) from it. The linguistic proof is that 'ḥayḍah' (with the feminine tā' marbūṭah) denotes a single complete instance of menstruation. The completeness of a menstruation is not achieved by the bleeding alone but by its conclusion which is the state of purity. This is supported by a reference to the hadith of istibra' (where a man is instructed to wait until one complete menstruation to verify clearance of pregnancy). The commentary emphasizes that 'hayḍah' implies the entire menstrual period including the cessation of blood and the subsequent ritual purity (ṭuhr). Thus, the condition is only fulfilled when she becomes clean after that menstruation ends.

Key Terms
حیضہ (ḥayḍah): A single complete menstruation, which includes the entire bleeding period and ends with ritual purification (ṭuhr).
طہر (ṭuhr): Purity; the state when menstrual bleeding ceases and a woman performs ghusl or the bleeding stops, marking the end of hayd.

Key Takeaway

Conditional Divorce and the Minimum Duration of Menstruation
Explains that mere spotting does not trigger divorce; three continuous days of menstrual blood are required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional divorce linked to menstruation and explain the three-day minimum requirement.

Core Idea
No divorce until three continuous days of menstrual blood—a single spot does not fulfill the condition.

A husband conditions divorce on his wife menstruating, but she only sees a spot of blood. Does divorce occur? Not according to the Hanafi school—because the minimum for menstruation is three days and nights. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional divorce scenario
The husband says 'When you menstruate, you are divorced.' This creates a suspended divorce (talaq mu'allaq) contingent on the wife actually menstruating.
2
Apply the Hanafi definition of menstruation
In the Hanafi school, the minimum duration of true menstruation (hayd) is three continuous days and nights. Bleeding less than that is istihadah (non-menstrual discharge).
3
Determine when the condition is fulfilled
The condition is fulfilled only when blood flows for three full days. If it stops earlier, it was not hayd, so no divorce occurs. Once three days are complete, we rule that she was menstruating from the start, and the divorce takes effect retroactively.
This retroactive effect is based on the legal principle that continuity proves the blood was from the womb.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds a minimum of 24 hours for menstruation. Thus, under Shafi'i fiqh, a one-day flow could trigger the condition. The practical effect (thamarah al-khilaf) is that the timing of divorce differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر نے کہا اذا حضت فانت طالق عورت نے خون دیکھا طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی یہاں تک کہ تین دن تک خون جاری رہے
واذاقال لها اذاحضت فانت طالق فرأت الدم لم يقع الطلاق حتى يستمر ثلثة ايام لان ما ينقطع دونه لا يكون حيضا فاذاتمت ثلثة ايام حكمنا بالطلاق من حين حاضت لانه بالامتداد عرف انه من الرحم فكان حيضا من الابتداء

If the husband said: 'When you menstruate, you are divorced,' and the woman saw blood, divorce does not occur until blood continues for three days. Because what stops before that is not menstruation. When three days are completed, we rule that divorce occurred from the time she started menstruating, because by continuity it is known that the blood is from the womb, so it was menstruation from the beginning. Explanation: If the husband said to his wife 'When you menstruate, you are divorced,' and the woman saw blood, mere sighting of blood does not cause divorce until blood continues for three full days. The proof is that in our school the minimum duration of menstruation is three days and three nights. Blood that stops within less than that period is not menstruation but istihadah. However, if full three days of blood occurred, divorce is ruled from the beginning of bleeding because the continuity indicates it is uterine blood, so it is considered menstruation from the start.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding conditional divorce linked to menstruation. The author first states the ruling: if a husband says 'When you menstruate, you are divorced' and the wife sees blood, divorce does not occur until the blood continues for three full days. The Arabic text provides the reasoning: blood that stops before three days is not menstruation; upon completion of three days, we rule that she was menstruating from the beginning, so divorce takes effect from the start of bleeding. The Urdu commentary expands: mere spotting does not trigger divorce; the minimum menstrual period in the Hanafi school is three days and three nights. Blood lasting less is istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding). If three days are completed, the divorce is effective from the first appearance of blood because continuity proves it is menstrual. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that the minimum menstruation is three days, and conditional divorces are determined accordingly.

Key Terms
حیض (hayd): Menstrual blood that flows for a minimum of three days and nights.
اقل مدت حیض (aqall muddat al-hayd): The minimum duration of menstruation: three days and three nights.
طلاق (talaq): Divorce; termination of marriage by the husband's pronouncement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a conditional divorce linked to menstruation only takes effect if the wife experiences three continuous days of menstrual blood.

Conditional Divorce on a Menstrual Period: Requires Completion of Purity
States that when the condition uses 'haydah' (a period), divorce occurs only after the woman becomes pure from that menstruation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional divorce using the term 'haydah', explain the linguistic and hadith-based reasoning, and apply it to similar conditional statements.

Core Idea
A conditional divorce tied to 'a menstrual period' (haydah) takes effect only when the woman becomes pure, because 'haydah' means the complete cycle ending with purity.

Conditional divorces often hinge on precise wording. In Hanafi law, when a husband says 'When you have a menstrual period, you are divorced,' the timing of the divorce depends on whether 'haydah' refers to the bleeding alone or the entire cycle. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, which relies on linguistic analysis and a key hadith, to show why divorce occurs at the moment of purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is a conditional divorce (talaq mu'allaq) using the phrase 'idha hidti haydatan fa-anti taliq'. The Hanafi ruling is that divorce does not occur until the woman becomes pure (tuhr) from that specific menstruation.
2
Locate the Dalil (Evidence)
The author cites the hadith of istibra' from Sunan Abi Dawud: 'لا توطاء الحبالي حتى يضعن حملهن ولا الحبالى حتى يستبر أن بحيضة' – which commands waiting for one 'haydah' before intercourse with a purchased slave-girl. This hadith defines 'haydah' as a complete period.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning (dalala) is considered qat'i in this context.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (Indication)
The word 'haydah' (with the taa marbuta) in Arabic indicates completeness. The hadith uses it to require a full cycle, which ends with purity. Therefore, the same meaning applies to the divorce condition – the condition is fulfilled only at the onset of purity.
Linguistic principle: the taa often denotes a single instance, but in 'haydah' it signifies a complete unit.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Disagreement)
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may interpret 'haydah' as the bleeding period alone, so divorce would occur at the start of bleeding. The Hanafi school rejects this based on the hadith and Arabic usage.
Cross-madhhab status: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) because it aligns with the linguistic norm and the explicit hadith. No intra-Hanafi disagreement exists on this point.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

اگر شوہر نے کہا اذا حضت حيضة فانت طالق عورت کو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی یہاں تک کہ عورت حیض سے پاک ہو جائے

ترجمہ اور اگر عورت سے کہا کہ جب تو حائضہ ہو ایک حیض کر کے تو تو طالقہ ہے تو یہ عورت ) طالقہ نہ ہوگی ۔ یہاں تک کہ اس حیض سے پاک ہو جائے کیونکہ حیضتہ باء تاء) کے ساتھ حیض کامل ہے اور اسی وجہ سے حیض کامل پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ حدیث استبراء میں ۔ اور حیض کا کمال اس کی انتہا سے ہوتا ہے اور انتہا طہر سے ہوگی ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا اذا حضت حيضة فانتِ طالق تو یہ عورت مطلقہ نہ ہوگی ۔ یہاں تک کہ اپنے اس حیض سے پاک ہو جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حیضہ بالتا حیض کامل کو کہتے ہیں۔ اور حیض کا کمال اس کے ختم ہونے سے ہوگا اور ختم ہونا طہر سے ہوگا۔ اس وجہ سے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ طبر شروع ہونے پر طلاق واقع ہوگی اس سے پہلے نہیں ۔ اسی وجہ سے حدیث استبراء میں بھی حريضہ کو حیض کامل پر محمول کیا گیا ہے حدیث استبراء سے مراد یہ حدیث ہے لا توطاء الحبالي حتى يضعن حملهن ولا الحبالى حتى يستبر أن بحيضة (رواه ابو داؤد في سننه) - حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا حاملہ عورتوں سے وطی نہ کی جائے یہاں تک کہ وہ اپنے حمل کو وضع کر دیں اور نہ ولی کی جائے غیر حاملہ عورتوں سے یہاں تک کہ ایک حیض کامل کے ساتھ استبراء کریں۔ اس حدیث میں حیضہ سے مراد کامل حیض ہے۔ عنایہ یعنی شرح ہدایہ)
And if he said to her: 'When you have a menstrual period, you are divorced,' she is not divorced until she becomes pure from that menstruation, because 'haydah' with the ta' indicates complete menstruation, and for this reason it is interpreted as such in the hadith of istibra'. Its completion is by its end, and that is by purity. Explanation: If a man says to his wife 'When you have a menstrual period, you are divorced,' she is not divorced until she becomes pure from that menstruation. The proof is that 'haydah' denotes a complete menstrual period. Completeness of menstruation is by its termination, and termination is by purity. Therefore, divorce occurs at the onset of purity, not before. Likewise, in the hadith of istibra', 'haydah' is interpreted as a complete period. The hadith: 'Do not have intercourse with pregnant women until they deliver, nor with non-pregnant women until they complete one complete menstrual period (istibra').' In this hadith, 'haydah' means complete menstruation.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning conditional divorce using the term 'haydah' (a menstrual period). The author rules that if a husband says 'When you have a menstrual period, you are divorced,' divorce does not occur until the woman becomes pure from that menstruation. The Arabic text explains that 'haydah' with the taa indicates complete menstruation, and its completion is marked by purity. The Urdu commentary elaborates: the word 'haydah' (with the taa) in Arabic signifies a complete cycle. Therefore, the condition is fulfilled only at the end of the menstrual period when purity (tuhr) begins. The author cites the hadith of istibra' (waiting for one menstrual period before intercourse after purchase of a slave-girl) where 'haydah' is also interpreted as complete menstruation. This establishes that the term 'haydah' always means a full period, and its completion is at the time of purity. Thus, divorce takes effect at the start of purity, not during bleeding.

Key Terms
حيضة (haydah): A complete menstrual period, including its end by purity.
طهر (tuhur): Purity from menstruation; the state after bleeding stops and ghusl is performed.
استبراء (istibra'): Waiting for one menstrual period to ensure a woman is not pregnant.
