Conditional Divorce on Fasting: The Role of 'Yawm'
Distinguishes between conditional divorce on 'fasting a day' (divorce at sunset) and on 'fasting' (divorce as soon as fast is valid).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi rulings on conditional divorce phrased as 'if you fast a day' versus 'if you fast,' and state the precise moment of divorce in each case.

Core Idea
'Yawm' in conditional divorce on fasting means full daylight; without it, any valid fast triggers divorce.

In Hanafi law, the precise wording of a conditional divorce determines the moment when the condition is fulfilled. This lesson examines a key distinction: when a husband says 'if you fast a day' versus 'if you fast' (without specifying a day). The linguistic interpretation of 'yawm' (day) in conjunction with an extended action like fasting leads to different outcomes. Understanding this allows you to apply the correct ruling in similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two phrasings: (1) 'if you fast a day' and (2) 'if you fast' without specifying 'day'. Note that the first includes the word 'yawm' while the second does not.
2
Analyze the linguistic rule for 'yawm'
When 'yawm' is conjoined with an extended action (e.g., fasting), the Hanafis interpret it to mean the entire daylight period (from dawn to sunset), not just any part of the day. This rule is based on customary usage.
Extended actions are those that naturally span time, like fasting, praying, or staying.
3
Apply the rule to the first scenario
Since 'yawm' means the full day, the condition is only fulfilled when she fasts the entire day until sunset. Therefore, divorce occurs at sunset of the day she fasts.
She must have the intention for the whole day; even a partial fast does not trigger divorce.
4
Contrast the second scenario
When 'yawm' is omitted, the condition is not measured by any standard duration. As soon as she performs a valid fast (even a short while) with its rukn and shart, the condition is met and divorce occurs immediately.
The rukn of fasting is abstaining from food, drink, and intercourse; the shart includes intention and purity from menstruation.
5
Recognize the role of rukn and shart
The passage emphasizes that in the second scenario, fasting is 'found with its rukn and shart' – meaning that any act that qualifies as a valid fast, regardless of duration, suffices to trigger the condition.
This highlights that the husband's unspecified 'fast' refers to the essential reality of fasting, not a measured portion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر نے کہا انت طالق اذا صمت يوماً سورج غروب ہونے پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی
واذا قالت انت طالق اذا صمت يوما طلقت حين تغيب الشمس فى اليوم الذى تصوم لان اليوم اذاقرن بفعل ممتد يراد به بياض النهار بخلاف ماذا قال لها اذا صمت لانه لم يقدره بمعيار وقد وجد الصوم بركنه وشرطه
ترجمہ اور جب کہا تو طالقہ ہے جب تو نے ایک دن کا روزہ رکھا تو آفتاب غروب ہوتے ہی مطلقہ ہو جائے گی اس دن میں جس دن روزہ رکھے گی ۔ کیونکہ یوم جب فعل ممتد کے ساتھ مقترن ہو تو اس سے بیاض نہار مراد ہوتا ہے۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ عورت سے کہا جب تو روزہ رکھے۔ کیونکہ روزہ کو کسی معیار کے ساتھ مقدر نہیں کیا ہے اور روزہ اپنے رکن اور شرط کے ساتھ پایا گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی سے انت طالق اذا صمت يوماً کہا پھر اس عورت نے روزہ رکھا تو جس دن روزہ رکھا اس دن سورج غروب ہوتے ہی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل قاعدہ ہے کہ لفظ یوم فعل ممتد کے ساتھ مقرن ہو تو یوم سے مراد بیان نہار ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مطلق وقت ۔ اور یہاں صوم فعل ممتد ہے لہذا یوم سے مراد بیاض نہار ہوگا۔ اور وقوع طلاق کیلئے غروب تک پورے دن کا روزہ رکھنا شرط ہوگا۔ پس شرط پائے جاتے ہی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ اور یہی حکم ہے انت طالق اذا صمت صوماً کا۔
اس کے برخلاف اگر شوہر نے انت طالق اذا صمت کہا بغیر لفظ یوم ذکر کیئے تو اگر عورت نے بنیت صوم تھوڑی دیر کا روزہ رکھ لیا تب بھی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ شوہر نے روزہ کو کسی معیار یعنی یوم وغیرہ کے مقدر نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور مطلقا روزہ اپنے رکن اور شرط کے ساتھ پایا گیا۔ اس وجہ سے طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ روزہ کا رکن کھانے پینے اور جماع سے رکنا ہے اور شرط نیت اور حیض و نفاس سے پاک ہونا ہے۔
And if he said: 'You are divorced when you fast a day,' she is divorced at sunset on the day she fasts, because 'yawm' when conjoined with an extended action refers to the daylight period. Unlike if he said 'when you fast' without specifying a day, because he did not measure it with a standard, and fasting is found with its rukn and shart. Explanation: If a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced when you fast a day,' and she fasts, then divorce occurs at sunset of that day. The rule is that the word 'yawm' when linked to an extended action means daytime, not absolute time. Here fasting is an extended action, so 'yawm' means daylight. For divorce to occur, she must fast the entire day until sunset. When the condition is fulfilled, divorce occurs. The same applies to 'you are divorced if you fast a fast.' On the contrary, if the husband says 'You are divorced if you fast' without mentioning 'day,' then even if she fasts for a short while with the intention of fasting, divorce occurs. Because he did not assign any standard (like a day) and fasting is found with its rukn (abstaining from food, drink, and intercourse) and shart (intention and purity from menstruation/postpartum bleeding).
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning conditional divorce linked to fasting. The author distinguishes two scenarios: First, if the husband says 'You are divorced when you fast a day,' divorce occurs at sunset of that day. The Arabic text explains that 'yawm' (day) when paired with an extended action (such as fasting) means daylight, not a mere point in time. Therefore, she must fast the entire day; divorce takes effect at sunset. The Urdu commentary adds that the same applies to 'you are divorced if you fast a fast' because 'sawman' implies a complete fasting day. Second, if the husband says only 'if you fast' without specifying 'day,' then even a short period of fasting with intention suffices, because the condition is unmeasured and fasting exists with its essential elements (rukn) and conditions (shart). The rukn of fasting is abstaining from eating, drinking, and marital relations; the shart includes intention and freedom from menstruation/postpartum bleeding. This highlights the importance of wording in conditional divorces.

Key Terms
یوم (yawm): When linked to an extended action (e.g., fasting), it means the daylight period from dawn to sunset.
صوم (sawm): Fasting; abstaining from eating, drinking, and intercourse with intention.
ركن (rukn): Essential element; for fasting, it is abstaining from food, drink, and intercourse.
بیناض نہار (bayad al-nahar): The daylight period from dawn to sunset.

Key Takeaway
When 'yawm' is mentioned in a conditional divorce involving fasting, divorce occurs only at the end of the full daylight fast; without 'yawm', any valid fast triggers immediate divorce.

Conditional Divorce on Birth of Twins: The Ruling When Order is Unknown
Ruling on conditional divorce with twins and unknown birth order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for conditional divorce when twins are born with unknown order, and apply the distinction between qada (court ruling) and tanazzuh (religious caution).

Core Idea
When the order of twins' birth is unknown, the court enforces one divorce, but religious caution requires observing two divorces.

Conditional divorce scenarios often involve complex determinations of timing. When a husband attaches different numbers of divorces to the birth of a boy versus a girl, and the wife gives birth to twins of both sexes without knowing which came first, Hanafi fiqh provides a practical ruling that balances judicial certainty with religious scrupulousness. This lesson examines that ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The husband's statement creates two separate conditional divorces: one divorce if a boy is born, two divorces if a girl is born.
The condition is attached to the event of birth, not the number of children.
2
Identify the factual uncertainty
The wife gives birth to both a boy and a girl, but the order of birth is unknown. This uncertainty affects which conditions are triggered and in what sequence.
The order matters because the iddah may end after the first birth, preventing subsequent divorces.
3
Apply the ruling in court (qada)
In a court of law, the judge enforces only one divorce. This is because the minimum that can be certain is that at least one divorce occurred (if the boy was first). The court cannot enforce two divorces without proof of the order.
The court relies on apparent evidence; it does not impose religious caution.
4
Apply the ruling in private (tanazzuh)
For religious scrupulousness, the wife must consider herself divorced twice. This is because there is a possibility that the girl was born first, triggering two divorces. To avoid potential sin (remaining married after a divorce that may have occurred), she must observe the stricter possibility.
Tanazzuh is a personal religious obligation, not a legal ruling enforced by the court.
5
Understand the reasoning
The reasoning considers two scenarios. If the boy was born first, one divorce occurs, and the iddah ends with the second birth (the girl), so no further divorce can occur. If the girl was born first, two divorces occur. Since the order is unknown, the safer option is to assume the scenario that results in more divorces for religious caution.
The iddah of a pregnant woman ends with delivery of all children; if the iddah has ended, a later divorce is ineffective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر نے بیوی سے کہا اذا ولدت غلاما فانت طالق واحدة واذا ولدت جارية فانت طالق ثنتین لڑکا اور لڑکی دونوں کو جنا کتنی طلاقیں واقع ہونگی
و من قال لامرأته اذا ولدت غلاما فانت طالق واحدة واذا ولدت جارية فانت طالق ثنتين فولدت غلاما وجارية و لا يدرى ايهما اول لزمه فى القضاء تطليقة وفي التنزه تطليقتان وانقضت العدة لانها لو ولدت الغلام اولا وقعت واحدة وتنقضى عدتها بوضع الجارية ثم لاتقع أخرى به لانه حال انقضاء العدة ولو ولدت الجارية
And whoever said to his wife: 'If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced once, and if you give birth to a girl, you are divorced twice,' and she gives birth to both a boy and a girl without knowing which came first: in court one divorce is enforced, and in scrupulousness two divorces are enforced, and her iddah ends (with the second birth). Because if she gave birth to the boy first, one divorce occurs, and her iddah ends by delivering the girl; then no further divorce occurs because she is in the state of completed iddah. But if she gave birth to the girl first, then... (text incomplete).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling regarding a complex conditional divorce scenario where the husband attaches different numbers of divorces to the birth of a boy versus a girl, and the wife gives birth to twins of both sexes without known order. The Arabic text (and initial Urdu) provides the ruling: in judicial matters (qada), one divorce is enforced; for religious scrupulousness (tanazzuh), two divorces are considered binding to avoid potential sin. The reasoning is based on probabilities: if the boy was born first, one divorce occurs upon his birth, then the iddah ends with the delivery of the girl (because iddah of childbirth ends with delivery of all children), so no further divorce can occur. If the girl was born first, two divorces occur, and then the boy's birth might add? The text is cut off, but the intended ruling is clear: the safest option is to observe two divorces. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle of caution (ihtiyat) in unclear situations.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Judicial ruling; what a judge enforces based on apparent evidence.
تنزه (tanazzuh): Scrupulousness; avoiding potential sin by adopting the stricter view.
عدة (iddah): Waiting period after divorce or death before remarriage; for a pregnant woman, ends with delivery.

Conditional Divorce on Fasting: The Role of Specifying a Day
Ruling on conditional divorce with and without specifying a day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditional divorce when 'day' is specified vs. not, and state the precise moment divorce occurs in each case.

Core Idea
When 'day' is specified with fasting, divorce requires a full daylight fast; without, any fasting fulfills.

In conditional divorce, the wording determines the condition's scope. This passage examines two scenarios: 'if you fast a day' and 'if you fast'. The Hanafi school applies a linguistic principle that 'day' when tied to an extended action means the entire daylight period. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying suspended divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Locate the two phrases: 'if you fast a day' and 'if you fast' (without day). Note that the first includes a time quantifier, the second does not.
The quantifier is the key variable.
2
Understand the linguistic principle
The word 'yawm' (day) when coupled with an extended action (like fasting) refers to the full daylight period, not a point in time.
This is a Hanafi principle of interpretation.
3
Apply the rukn and shart of fasting
Fasting's essential element (rukn) is abstention from food, drink, and sex; its condition (shart) includes intention and purity. In the unspecified case, any act meeting these suffices.
No minimum duration is required without a quantifier.
4
Derive the ruling
With 'day': divorce at sunset of the day she fasts completely. Without 'day': divorce upon any valid fasting, even a short time.
The difference turns on whether the condition is quantified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر نے کہا: انت طالق اذا صمت يوماً، سورج غروب ہونے پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔
واذا قالت: انت طالق اذا صمت يوما، طلقت حين تغيب الشمس فى اليوم الذى تصوم، لان اليوم اذاقرن بفعل ممتد يراد به بياض النهار، بخلاف ماذا قال لها: اذا صمت، لانه لم يقدره بمعيار، وقد وجد الصوم بركنه وشرطه۔
ترجمہ: اور جب کہا: تو طالق ہے جب تو نے ایک دن کا روزہ رکھا، تو آفتاب غروب ہوتے ہی مطلقہ ہو جائے گی اس دن میں جس دن روزہ رکھے گی۔ کیونکہ یوم جب فعل ممتد کے ساتھ مقترن ہو تو اس سے بیاض نہار مراد ہوتا ہے۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ عورت سے کہا: جب تو روزہ رکھے۔ کیونکہ روزہ کو کسی معیار کے ساتھ مقدر نہیں کیا ہے اور روزہ اپنے رکن اور شرط کے ساتھ پایا گیا۔ تشریح: اگر شوہر نے اپنی بیوی سے انت طالق اذا صمت يوماً کہا پھر اس عورت نے روزہ رکھا تو جس دن روزہ رکھا اس دن سورج غروب ہوتے ہی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل قاعدہ ہے کہ لفظ یوم فعل ممتد کے ساتھ مقرن ہو تو یوم سے مراد بیاض نہار ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مطلق وقت۔ اور یہاں صوم فعل ممتد ہے لہذا یوم سے مراد بیاض نہار ہوگا۔ اور وقوع طلاق کیلئے غروب تک پورے دن کا روزہ رکھنا شرط ہوگا۔ پس شرط پائے جاتے ہی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اور یہی حکم ہے انت طالق اذا صمت صوماً کا۔
اس کے برخلاف اگر شوہر نے انت طالق اذا صمت کہا بغیر لفظ یوم ذکر کیئے تو اگر عورت نے بنیت صوم تھوڑی دیر کا روزہ رکھ لیا تب بھی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ شوہر نے روزہ کو کسی معیار یعنی یوم وغیرہ کے مقدر نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور مطلقا روزہ اپنے رکن اور شرط کے ساتھ پایا گیا۔ اس وجہ سے طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ روزہ کا رکن کھانے پینے اور جماع سے رکنا ہے اور شرط نیت اور حیض و نفاس سے پاک ہونا ہے۔
The husband said: 'You are divorced if you fast one day' — divorce will occur at sunset. And if he said: 'You are divorced if you fast one day', she is divorced at sunset of the day she fasts, because 'day' when coupled with an extended action refers to the white daylight, unlike if he said to her 'if you fast', because he did not quantify it with a measure, and fasting was found with its rukn and shart. Translation: And when he said: 'You are divorced if you fast one day', then she becomes divorced at sunset of that day on which she will fast. Because 'day' when associated with an extended action signifies the daylight. Contrary to the case when he said to the woman: 'If you fast', because fasting was not quantified with a standard, and fasting was found with its rukn and shart. Explanation: If the husband said to his wife 'You are divorced if you fast one day' and then the woman fasted, then on that day at sunset divorce will occur. The principle is that the word 'day' when associated with an extended action means daylight, not absolute time. And here fasting is an extended action, so 'day' means daylight. For divorce to occur, fasting the whole day until sunset is a condition. So when the condition is met, divorce occurs. The same ruling applies to 'You are divorced if you fast a fasting'. Conversely, if the husband said 'You are divorced if you fast' without mentioning 'day', then if the woman fasts for a short while with the intention of fasting, divorce still occurs. Because the husband did not quantify fasting with any standard like a day. And absolutely, fasting was found with its rukn and shart. Hence divorce occurs. The rukn of fasting is refraining from eating, drinking, and intercourse, and the shart is intention and being free from menstruation and postpartum bleeding.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings on conditional divorce related to fasting. The first ruling: when the husband says 'if you fast one day', divorce only occurs after she completes the entire day until sunset. The reason is that the word 'yawm' (day) when linked to an extended action (like fasting) refers to the full daylight period. The second ruling: when the husband says simply 'if you fast' without specifying a day, any amount of fasting, even a short while, fulfills the condition and divorce occurs immediately upon that minimal fasting. The distinction is based on whether the condition is quantified or not. The rukn (pillar) of fasting is abstention from food, drink, and sex; the shart (condition) is intention and purity from menstruation. This ruling follows the Hanafi principle that when an action is mentioned without qualification, it is fulfilled by its essence.

Key Terms
يوم (yawm): When used with an extended action, it means the full daylight period (bayad al-nahar).
رکن (rukn): The essential element of fasting: refraining from eating, drinking, and intercourse.
شرط (shart): Condition for valid fasting: intention and freedom from menses/postpartum bleeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced if you fast' (without mentioning a day), and she fasts for one hour with intention, what is the ruling?
A) Divorce does not occur until she completes the full day
B) Divorce occurs immediately after that hour
C) Divorce occurs only if she fasts the entire day
D) Divorce depends on her intention

Key Takeaway
The wording of a conditional divorce determines the exact fulfillment required; always analyze the presence of quantifiers like 'day'.

Talaq — Divorce

Judicial and Precautionary Rulings in Conditional Divorce with Unknown Order
Ruling on multiple conditional divorces with unknown order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the judicial (qada') and precautionary (tanzih) rulings for a conditional divorce when the order of births is unknown, and explain the reasoning based on certainty and doubt.

Core Idea
Certainty requires one divorce judicially; precaution recommends two.

This passage addresses a complex scenario where a husband conditions divorce on the birth of a child, with different numbers for a boy (one) and a girl (two). When the wife delivers both and the order is unknown, two valid possibilities exist, each yielding a different number of divorces. The Hanafi school resolves this by applying the legal maxim that certainty (yaqeen) is not overridden by doubt (shakk). Thus, in court (qada'), the minimal certain number—one divorce—is enforced. Out of personal piety (tanzih), however, the woman should observe two divorces to be safe in the sight of Allah. The passage also clarifies that the iddah ends with the last birth, regardless of order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the husband's statement and possible outcomes
Recognize that the husband made two conditional pronouncements: 'If boy, one divorce; if girl, two divorces.' The wife delivers both a boy and a girl. The key variable is the order of births, which is unknown.
Each order leads to a different number of divorces: boy first → one; girl first → two.
2
Determine what is certain and what is doubtful
In either scenario, at least one divorce certainly occurs (in both orders, one divorce is effective: if boy first, that one; if girl first, the first of the two). The second divorce only occurs in one scenario (girl first). Therefore, one divorce is certain, the second is doubtful.
Certainty: one divorce. Doubt: whether the second occurred.
3
Apply the legal maxim 'al-yaqeen la yazulu bi al-shakk'
Knowing that one divorce is certain and the second is doubtful, the court enforces only the certain one. Doubt cannot establish a legal right or obligation in judicial matters.
This is a fundamental Hanafi principle in evidence and rulings.
4
Distinguish between qada' (judicial) and tanzih (piety)
For court enforcement (qada'), only one divorce is recognized because it is certain. However, for personal religious observance (tanzih), the woman should act as if two divorces occurred, out of caution (ihtiyat). This is recommended, not legally binding.
Tanzih is a moral recommendation, not a legal obligation.
5
Understand the iddah ruling
In both possible orders, the iddah ends with the birth of the second child (whether boy or girl), because the iddah of a pregnant woman concludes with delivery. Since both children are delivered, the iddah is certainly complete.
No further divorces can occur after the iddah ends, regardless of the number.

و من قال لامرأته: اذا ولدت غلاما فانت طالق واحدة، واذا ولدت جارية فانت طالق ثنتين، فولدت غلاما وجارية و لا يدرى ايهما اول، لزمه فى القضاء تطليقة، وفي التنزه تطليقتان، وانقضت العدة. لانها لو ولدت الغلام اولا وقعت واحدة وتنقضى عدتها بوضع الجارية ثم لا تقع اخرى به لانه حال انقضاء العدة. ولو ولدت الجارية اولا وقعت تطليقتان وانقضت عدتها بوضع الغلام ثم لا يقع شئ اخر به لما ذكرنا انه حال انقضا. فاذا في حال يقع واحدة وفي حال يقع ثنتان فلا تقع الثانية بالشك والاحتمال، والاولى ان ناخذ بالثنتين تنزها واحتياطا، والعدة منقضية بيقين لما بينا.
ترجمہ: اور جس شخص نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا: اگر تو نے لڑکا جنا تو تو طالق بیک طلاق ہے، اور اگر لڑکی جنی تو تو طالق بدو طلاق ہے۔ پس اس عورت نے لڑکا اور لڑکی دونوں جنے اور معلوم نہیں کہ پہلا کون ہے، تو اس کو قضاء ایک طلاق لازم ہوئی اور تنزہاً دو طلاقیں لازم ہوں گی، اور عدت گزر گئی۔ کیونکہ اگر پہلے لڑکا جنا تو ایک واقع ہوئی اور اس کی عدت لڑکی جننے سے گزر گئی، پھر دوسری واقع نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ وہ عدت گزرنے کا وقت ہے۔ اور اگر پہلے لڑکی جنی تو دو طلاقیں واقع ہوگئیں اور اس کی عدت لڑکا جننے سے پوری ہوگئی، پھر اس کی وجہ سے دوسری واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے کہ وہ عدت گزرنے کا وقت ہے۔ پس اس وقت ایک حالت میں ایک واقع ہوگی اور ایک حالت میں دو واقع ہوں گی۔ پس دوسری شک اور احتمال کی وجہ سے واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اولیٰ یہ ہے کہ ہم دو کو اختیار کریں تنزہاً اور احتیاطاً۔ اور عدت بالیقین ختم ہوگئی اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا: اذا ولدت غلاماً فانت طالق واحدة و اذا ولدت جارية فانت طالق ثنتين۔ اسکے بعد اس عورت نے لڑکا اور لڑکی دونوں کو جنا تو اس مسئلہ میں چند صورتیں ہیں:
(۱) اگر یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ لڑکے کی ولادت پہلے ہوئی تو ایک طلاق واقع ہوئی اور اس عورت کی عدت لڑکی کی ولادت سے پوری ہوگئی کیونکہ حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہوتی ہے اور اس کے بعد کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔
(۲) اور اگر یہ معلوم ہے کہ لڑکی کی ولادت پہلے ہوئی تو دو طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی۔
(۳) اور اگر زوجین میں اختلاف ہو گیا مثلاً شوہر کہتا ہے کہ لڑکے کی ولادت پہلے ہوئی اور بیوی کہتی ہے کہ لڑکی کی ولادت پہلے ہوئی تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ زیادتی طلاق کا منکر ہے۔
(۴) اور اگر معلوم نہیں کہ پہلے کس کی ولادت ہوئی جیسا کہ کتاب کا مسئلہ ہے تو اس صورت میں قضاء ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ایک کا واقع ہونا یقینا ثابت ہے اور دوسری کے واقع ہونے میں شک ہے۔ البتہ دیاتھا اور نزدھا دو طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی۔ دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ اگر اولا غلام کی ولادت ہوئی تو ایک طلاق واقع ہو گئی اور جاریہ جننے کی وجہ سے اس کی عدت گذر گئی۔ کیونکہ لڑکا جننے کے بعد یہ عورت حاملہ ہے اور حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہے پھر اس وضع جاریہ سے اور کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہو گی۔ اسلئے کہ یہ وقت انقضاء عدت کا وقت ہے اور انقضاء عدت کا وقت زوال نکاح کا وقت ہے۔ اور زائل زوال کے وقت کچھ عمل نہیں کرتا ہے۔ اور اگر جاریہ کی ولادت اولا ہوئی تو دو طلاقیں ہوں گی۔ اور وضع غلام سے اس کی عدت پوری ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ یہ عورت جاریہ کی ولادت کے بعد حاملہ ہے اور حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہے۔ پھر اس وضع غلام سے دوسری کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے کہ یہ انقضاء عدت کا وقت ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ ایک حالت میں ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی اور ایک حالت میں دو واقع ہوں گی۔ پس ایک کا واقع ہونا بالیقین ہے اور دوسری کے واقع ہونے میں شک اور احتمال ہے اور شک کی وجہ سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی۔ اس وجہ سے قضاء ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ اور بہتر یہ
And whoever said to his wife: 'If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced with one divorce; and if you give birth to a girl, you are divorced with two divorces,' and she gave birth to a boy and a girl and it is not known which was first, then in judicial ruling one divorce is binding, and in self-restraint two divorces are binding, and the iddah has expired. Because if she gave birth to the boy first, one divorce occurred and her iddah ends with the delivery of the girl, then no other divorce occurs by it because it is the time of iddah completion. And if she gave birth to the girl first, two divorces occurred and her iddah ends with the delivery of the boy, then nothing else occurs by it because of what we mentioned: it is the time of completion. So in one scenario one divorce occurs, and in another scenario two occur, so the second is not established due to doubt and probability. And it is better to take two out of self-restraint and caution. And the iddah is definitely concluded as we have explained. Translation: And whoever said to his wife: 'If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced with one divorce; and if you give birth to a girl, you are divorced with two divorces,' then that woman gave birth to both a boy and a girl, and it is not known which is first, then in judicial ruling one divorce is binding, and out of self-restraint two divorces are binding, and the iddah has passed. Because if she gave birth to the boy first, one divorce occurred and her iddah concludes with the delivery of the girl, then no second divorce occurs because it is the time of iddah completion. And if she gave birth to the girl first, two divorces occurred and her iddah concludes with the delivery of the boy, then no other occurs because of the same reason. So in one case one occurs, in another case two occur, so the second is not established due to doubt and probability, and it is better to take two out of self-restraint and caution, and the iddah is definitely concluded for the reason we mentioned. Explanation: The issue is that a man said to his wife: 'If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced with one divorce; and if you give birth to a girl, you are divorced with two divorces.' Then the woman gave birth to both a boy and a girl. In this issue there are several scenarios: (1) If it is known that the boy was born first, then one divorce occurred and her iddah concluded with the birth of the girl because the iddah of a pregnant woman is delivery, and no divorce occurs after that. (2) If it is known that the girl was born first, then two divorces occur. (3) If the spouses dispute, e.g., the husband says the boy was born first and the wife says the girl was born first, then the husband's word is accepted because he denies the extra divorce. (4) If it is not known which was born first, as in the book's issue, then in judicial ruling one divorce occurs because one is certainly established and the second is in doubt. However, according to piety and cautiousness, two divorces occur. The proof is that if the boy was born first, one divorce occurred and her iddah expired with the birth of the girl because she is pregnant after the boy, and the iddah of a pregnant woman is delivery, then no further divorce occurs by this delivery because it is the time of iddah completion, which is the time of dissolution of marriage, and a dissolving agent does not act at the time of dissolution. And if the girl was born first, two divorces occur and her iddah expires with the birth of the boy because she is pregnant after the girl, then no other divorce occurs by this delivery for the same reason. In summary, in one case one divorce occurs, in another case two occur. So one is certain, the second is doubtful, and divorce does not occur due to doubt. Therefore, in judicial ruling one divorce occurs. And it is better...
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage deals with a complex case of conditional divorce where the husband sets two different conditions with different outcomes: one divorce for a boy, two divorces for a girl. The woman gives birth to both but the order is unknown. The author outlines four scenarios: known order (boy first or girl first), dispute between spouses, and the main case where order is unknown. In the unknown order case, the ruling is: in court (qada'), only one divorce is effective because one divorce is certain and the second is doubtful. However, out of piety (tanzih) and caution (ihtiyat), the woman should consider herself to have been divorced twice. The reasoning is that if the boy came first, only one divorce occurs and the iddah ends with the girl's birth, so no second divorce; if the girl came first, two divorces occur and the iddah ends with the boy's birth. Since we don't know which scenario happened, we take the minimum (one) for legal enforcement, but the religiously cautious person would observe two. The iddah is definitely over in both scenarios, as the last birth completes it. The passage also mentions that if spouses dispute, the husband's word is taken because he denies the extra divorce (he is the defendant).

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Judicial ruling based on apparent evidence; here, one divorce is enforced in court.
تنزہ (tanzih): Self-restraint or piety; here, the woman should consider herself divorced twice out of caution.
عدت (iddah): Waiting period after divorce; for a pregnant woman, it ends with delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a husband says 'If boy, one divorce; if girl, two divorces' and the wife gives birth to both in unknown order, how many divorces are judicially enforced?
A) Two divorces
B) One divorce
C) No divorce, because the conditions are conditional
D) Three divorces, because both conditions are fulfilled

Key Takeaway
When order is unknown, the court enforces only the certain number of divorces (one), but out of piety the woman should observe two.

Conditional Divorce with Twins: Certainty vs Doubt
Ruling when twins born in unknown order under conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a conditional divorce involves twins of unknown birth order, apply the principle that certainty is not overridden by doubt, and distinguish between the judicial and cautionary rulings.

Core Idea
When the order of twins is unknown, only one talaq occurs judicially; caution recommends two.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with a subtle scenario in conditional divorce (talaq mu'allaq). A husband suspends divorce on the birth of a boy (one talaq) or a girl (two talaqs). When twins are born and the order of birth is unknown, we must determine how many divorces take effect. The key is the interaction between the condition and the idda (waiting period). This lesson walks through the reasoning using the Hanafi principle that certainty prevails over doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional divorce and the fact of twins
The husband said: boy = one talaq, girl = two talaqs. Twins born, order unknown.
Ta'liq (suspension) is valid in Hanafi law.
2
Analyze the effect of each possible order
If boy first: one talaq occurs, idda ends with girl's birth. If girl first: two talaqs occur, idda ends with boy's birth.
The idda of a pregnant woman ends with delivery (wad' al-haml).
3
Identify the certain and doubtful occurrences
In both scenarios, at least one talaq occurs. The second talaq occurs only if girl first. So occurrence of one is certain, occurrence of two is doubtful.
4
Apply the principle of yaqīn and shakk
Certainty (one talaq) is not overridden by doubt (second talaq). Therefore judicially only one talaq is effective.
Principle: 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk).
5
Note the cautionary recommendation
Out of piety (tanazzuhan) and caution (ihtiyatan), the couple should treat it as two talaqs to avoid any violation of the marriage.
This is not a judicial ruling but a recommended precaution.

کتاب الطلاق
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم اولا وقعت تطليقتان و انقضت عدتها بوضع الغلام ثم لا يقع شئى اخربه لما ذكرنا انه حال الانقضا فاذافي حال يقع واحدة وفى حال يقع ثنتان فلايقع الثانية بالشك والاحتمال والاولى ان ناخذ بالثنتين تنزها واحتياطا والعدة منقضية بيقين لما بينا
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ جب تو نے لڑ کا جنا تو ، تو طالقہ بیک طلاق ہے اور اگر لڑ کی جنی تو تو طالقہ بدو طلاق ہے۔ پس اس عورت نے لڑکا اور لڑکی دونوں جنے اور ( یہ ) معلوم نہیں کہ پہلا کون ہے تو اس کو قضاء ایک طلاق لازم ہوئی اور تنز با دو طلاقیں لازم ہوں گی ) اور عدت گزر گئی۔ کیونکہ اس نے پہلے لڑکا جنا تو ایک واقع ہوئی اور اس کی عدت گذر جائے گی لڑکی جاننے سے۔ پھر وضع جاریہ سے دوسری واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ وہ عدت گزرنے کا وقت ہے۔ اور اگر پہلے لڑکی جنی تو دو طلاقیں واقع ہوگئیں۔ اور اس کی عدت لڑکا جننے سے پوری ہو گئی۔ پھر اس کی وجہ سے دوسری واقع نہیں ہو گی۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے کہ (لڑکا جننے کا وقت ) عدت گزرنے کا وقت ہے۔ پس اس وقت ایک حالت میں ایک واقع ہوگی۔ اور ایک حالت میں دو واقع ہوں گی ۔ پس دوسری شک اور احتمال کی وجہ سے واقع نہیں ہوگی اور اولیٰ یہ ہے کہ ہم دو دو کو اختیار کریں تنز با اور احتیاطاً۔ اور عدت بالیقین ختم ہوگئی۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا اذا ولدت غلاماً فانت طالق واحدة و اذا ولدت جارية فانت طالق ثنتین ۔ اسکے بعد اس عورت نے لڑکا اور لڑکی دونوں کو جنا تو اس مسئلہ میں چند صورتیں ہیں،
۱) اگر یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ لڑکے کی ولادت پہلے ہوئی تو ایک طلاق واقع ہوئی اور اس عورت کی عدت لڑکی کی ولادت سے پوری ہوگئی کیونکہ حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہوتی ہے اور اس کے بعد کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔
(۲) اور اگر یہ معلوم ہے کہ لڑکی کی ولادت پہلے ہوئی تو دو طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی۔ (۳) اور اگر زوجین میں اختلاف ہو گیا مثلاً شوہر کہتا ہے کہ لڑکے کی ولادت پہلے ہوئی اور بیوی کہتی ہے کہ لڑکی کی ولادت پہلے ہوئی تو شوہر کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ زیادتی طلاق کا منکر ہے۔
۴) اور اگر معلوم نہیں کہ پہلے کس کی ولادت ہوئی جیسا کا کتاب کا مسئلہ ہے تو اس صورت میں قضاء ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ایک کا واقع ہونا یقینا ثابت ہے اور دوسری کے واقع ہونے کے میں شک ے۔ البتہ دیاتھا اور نزدھا دو طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی۔ دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ اگر اولا غلام کی ولادت ہوئی تو ایک طلاق واقع ہو گئی اور جار یہ جننے کی وجہ سے اس کی عدت گذر گئی۔ کیونکہ لڑکا جننے کے بعد یہ عورت حاملہ ہے اور حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہے پھر اس وضع جاریہ سے اور کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہو گی۔ اسلئے کہ یہ وقت انقضاء عدت کا وقت ہے اور انقضاء عدت کا وقت زوال نکاح کا وقت ہے۔ اور مزیل زوال کے وقت کچھ عمل نہیں کرتا ہے اور اگر جاریہ کی ولادت اولا ہوئی تو دو طلاقیں ہوں گی۔ اور وضع غلام سے اس کی عدت پوری ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ یہ عورت جاریہ کی ولادت کے بعد حاملہ ہے اور حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہے۔ پھر اس وضع غلام سے دوسری کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے کہ یہ انقضاء عدت کا وقت ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ ایک حالت میں ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی اور ایک حالت میں دو واقع ہوں گی۔ پس ایک کا واقع ہونا بالیقین ہے اور دوسری کے واقع ہونے میں شک اور احتمال ہے اور شک کی وجہ سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی۔ اس وجہ سے قضاء ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی ۔ اور بہتر یہ ہے کہ احتیاطاً دو واقع ہوں۔ اور عدت بالیقین گذرگئی سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے۔
Book of Divorce. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume 4. 'Initially, two divorces occurred and her idda ended with the birth of the boy, then nothing occurs...' because we mentioned that it is the time of completion [of idda]. So in one case one occurs and in another two occur, so the second does not occur due to doubt and probability. And it is better that we take the two as caution and precaution. And the idda is definitely completed as we clarified. Translation: And the man who said to his wife: 'When you give birth to a boy, you are divorced once, and if you give birth to a girl, you are divorced twice.' Then this woman gave birth to both a boy and a girl, and it is not known which was first. So judicially one divorce is necessary, and cautiously two divorces are necessary. And the idda ended. Because if she gave birth to the boy first, one occurred and her idda would be completed by the birth of the girl. Then by the birth of the girl, a second does not occur because it is the time of completion of idda. And if she gave birth to the girl first, then two divorces occurred, and her idda would be completed by the birth of the boy. Then by that, a second does not occur due to the evidence we mentioned that the time of birth is the time of completion of idda. So at that time, in one state one occurs, and in one state two occur. So the second does not occur due to doubt and probability. And it is better that we take the two as caution and precaution. And the idda is definitely ended as per the evidence we stated. Explanation: The issue is that a man said to his wife: 'If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced once, and if you give birth to a girl, you are divorced twice.' Then the woman gave birth to both a boy and a girl. There are several scenarios: 1) If it is known that the boy was born first, then one divorce occurred and the woman's idda was completed by the birth of the girl because the idda of a pregnant woman is delivery, and after that no divorce occurs. 2) If it is known that the girl was born first, then two divorces occur. 3) If the spouses dispute, e.g., the husband says the boy was born first and the wife says the girl was born first, the husband's statement is accepted because he denies an additional divorce. 4) If it is not known which was born first, as in the book's issue, then judicially one divorce occurs because one's occurrence is certainly established and there is doubt about the second. However, according to piety and caution, two divorces occur. The evidence: if the boy was born first, one divorce occurred and by the birth of the girl her idda ended because after the boy she was pregnant and the idda of a pregnant woman is delivery. Then by the birth of the girl no other divorce occurs because this is the time of completion of idda, and the time of completion of idda is the time of dissolution of marriage, and that which causes dissolution does not act at the time of dissolution. And if the girl was born first, then two divorces occur and by the birth of the boy her idda is completed because she becomes pregnant after the girl and the idda of a pregnant woman is delivery. Then by the birth of the boy no other divorce occurs due to the previous evidence that this is the time of completion of idda. Summary: In one state one divorce occurs, in another state two occur. So the occurrence of one is certain, and there is doubt and probability about the second. Due to doubt, divorce does not occur. Therefore judicially one divorce occurs. And it is better that cautiously two occur. And the idda definitely ended due to the previous evidence.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on the Hidayah by Imam Marghinani. The passage addresses a conditional divorce (talaq mu'allaq) where the husband suspends divorce on the birth of a boy (one talaq) or a girl (two talaqs). The wife gives birth to twins, and the order of birth is unknown. The text first gives the Arabic ruling from the Hidayah, then explains in Urdu. The key principle: the 'idda of a pregnant woman ends with delivery (wad' al-haml). When the first child is born, the conditional divorce triggers (one or two depending on the child's gender) and the 'idda begins. When the second child is born, that birth occurs after the 'idda has already ended, so no further divorce can occur because divorce cannot be effected after the marriage has already dissolved. Since the order is unknown, we have a conflict: if the boy was first, only one talaq occurred; if the girl was first, two occurred. The occurrence of one talaq is certain in both scenarios, but the second is doubtful. The Hanafi rule is that certainty (yaqin) is not overridden by doubt (shakk). Therefore, judicially (qada'an) only one talaq is effective. However, as a matter of piety (tanazzuhan) and caution (ihtiyatan), the couple should treat it as two talaqs. The text also discusses scenarios: if the order is known, that determines the number; if spouses dispute, the husband's word is taken because he denies an extra talaq.

Key Terms
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspending the occurrence of divorce on a future condition.
وقوع (wuqu'): The actual occurrence/effect of divorce when the condition is fulfilled.
عدت (idda): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband.
وضع حمل (wad' al-haml): Delivery of the child (birth).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says: 'If you give birth to a boy, you are divorced once; if to a girl, twice.' The wife gives birth to twins, but the order is unknown. What is the judicial (qada') ruling?
A) No divorce occurs at all.
B) One divorce occurs.
C) Two divorces occur.
D) Three divorces occur.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when doubt exists about the order of births in a conditional divorce, certainty of one divorce prevails, and judicially only one takes effect; caution suggests two.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
10 min
Conditional Divorce: Partial Fulfillment Inside Marriage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional divorce with partial fulfillment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority ruling when a conditional divorce is partially fulfilled outside marriage and partially inside, and explain the proof that the oath remains binding.

Core Idea
The oath (yamin) remains valid even after divorce; only the penalty's descent requires marriage at fulfillment.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about a conditional divorce. The husband suspends triple talaq on his wife speaking to two named persons. After giving one divorce and remarrying, the wife speaks to the first person while unmarried and to the second while married. The majority (Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students) hold that the triple talaq is triggered, while Imam Zufar disagrees. Understanding the distinction between the oath's continuity and the penalty's requirement clarifies a key principle in Hanafi conditional divorce law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Ruling in Question
Identify the key elements: conditional divorce on speaking to two persons, one divorce given, wife speaks to first person outside marriage, remarriage, then speaks to second person inside marriage. The dispute is whether the condition triggers talaq.
2
State the Majority Hanafi Position and Its Proof
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule that three talaqs occur. Their proof: the oath (yamin) remains valid after the first divorce because it resides in the dhimma; marriage is required only at the time of suspension and at the descent of the penalty, not in between.
See the argument using istishab al-hal and the concept of dhimma.
3
State Imam Zufar's Position and His Proof
Zufar holds no talaq occurs because he treats the two speeches as a single condition; since the first speech happened outside marriage, the entire condition fails. He analogizes it to other cases where partial fulfillment outside marriage voids the condition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response to Zufar
The Hanafi response is that the two speeches are not a single unit; the oath's validity is independent of ongoing marriage. Istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) supports the oath's survival. The condition is fulfilled when the second speech occurs within marriage.
The key distinction: the oath remains, the penalty only descends when marriage exists at the moment of fulfillment.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf) and the Mufta Bihi
Under Zufar's view, she is not divorced by the condition; under the majority, she becomes irrevocably divorced (a total of three talaqs after the first divorce, making her mughallazah). The mufta bihi is the majority view.
The text explicitly sides with the majority, stating 'lana' (our proof).

Source Text

شوہر نے منکوحہ سے کہا ان کلمت ابا عمرو ابا یوسف فانت طالق ثلاثا پھر ایک طلاق دے دی بائنہ ہوگئی اور اسکی عدت گزر گئی پھر اس نے ابو عمر سے اس حال میں کلام کی وہ اسکی بیوی نہیں تھی پھر عورت سے نکاح کر لیا پھر عورت نے ابو یوسف سے کلام کی اس حال میں کہ وہ بیوی ہے تو کتنی طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی
وان قال لها ان كلمت ابا عمرو وابا يوسف فانت طالق ثلاثا ثم طلقها واحدة فبانت وانقضت عدتها فكلمت ابا عمروثم تزوجها فكلمت ابايوسف فهي طالق ثلاثاً مع الواحدة الاولى وقال زفر لا يقع وهذه على وجوه اما ان وجد الشرطان فى الملك فيقع الطلاق وهذا ظاهر او وجدافی غیر الملک فلايقع او وجد الاول في الملک والثانی فی غیر الملک فلايقع ايضالان الجزاء لاینزل فی غیر الملک فلايقع او وجد الاول في غیر الملک والثانی فی الملک وهى مسالة الكتاب الخلافية له اعتبار الاول بالثاني اذهمافی حکم الطلاق کشیء واحدولنا ان صحة الكلام باهلية المتكلم الا ان الملك يشترط حالة التعليق ليصير الجزاء غالب الوجود لاستصحاب الجال فيصح اليمين وعند تمام الشرط لينزل الجزاء لانه لا ينزل الافی الملک و فيما بين ذلك الحال حال بقاء اليمين فيستغنى عن قيام الملک اذبقاؤه بمحله وهو الذمة
ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر نے اپنی منکوحہ سے کہا کہ اگر تو نے ابو عمر و وابو یوسف سے کلام کیا تو ، تو مطلقہ ثلاثہ ہے پھر اس کو ایک طلاق دے دی، سودہ بائنہ ہوگئی۔ اور اس کی عدت پوری ہوگئی ۔ پھر کلام کیا ابوعمرو سے پھر اس سے نکاح کیا پھر ابو یوسف سے کلام کیا تو یہ عورت مطلقہ ثلاث ہے پہلی ایک کے ساتھ ۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ تین واقع ہوں گی۔ اور یہ مسئلہ چند صورتوں پر ہے یا تو دونوں شرطیں ملک میں پائی جائیں گی۔ ( یعنی ابو عمرو اور ابو یوسف دونوں کے ساتھ بحالت نکاح کلام کرے گی ) تو طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ اور یہ ظاہر ہے یا دونوں غیر ملک میں پائی جائیں گی تو واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ یا اول ملک میں اور ثانی غیر ملک میں پائی جائے گی تو بھی واقع نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ جزاء غیر ملک میں نہیں اترتی پس واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ یا اول غیر ملک میں اور ثانی ملک میں پائی جائے گی اور یہی کتاب کا مختلف فیہ مسئلہ ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اول کا دوسری پر قیاس ہے اسلئے کہ دونوں طلاق کے حکم میں شی ء واحد کے مانند ہیں ۔ اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ کلام کا صیح ہونا متکلم کی لیاقت کے ساتھ ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ ملک کی شرط کی گئی تعلیق کے وقت۔ تا کہ جزاء غالب الوجود ہو سکے۔ استصحاب حال کیوجہ سے تا کہ قسم صحیح ہو ۔ اور شرط پوری ہونے کے وقت تا کہ جزاء اترے۔ کیونکہ جزا نہیں اترتی مگر ملک میں۔ اور ان دونوں کے درمیان بقاء یمین کی حالت ہے۔
پس قسم قیام ملک سے مستغنی ہوگی۔ اسلئے کہ قسم کی بقاء اپنے نمل کے ساتھ ہے اور وہ ( حالف کا ) ذمہ ہے۔ تشریح مسلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے اپنی منکوحہ سے کہا ان کلمت ابا عمرو با یوسف فانت طالق ثلاثاً ۔ پھر شوہر نے اس کو ایک طلاق دے دی۔ پس وہ بائنہ ہو گئی اور اس کی عدت پوری ہو گئی۔ پھر عورت نے ابو عمرو کے ساتھ اس حال میں کلام کیا کہ وہ بیوی نہیں ہے۔ پھر اس عورت کو نکاح میں لے لیا پھر اس عورت نے ابو یوسف کے ساتھ اس حال میں کلام کیا کہ وہ بیوی ہے تو اس صورت میں
The husband said to his wife: 'If you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf, you are divorced thrice.' Then he gave her one divorce; she became bain and her idda ended. Then she spoke to Abu Amr while she was not his wife. Then he married her. Then she spoke to Abu Yusuf while she was his wife. How many divorces occur? [Arabic portion:] And if he said to her: 'If you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf, you are divorced thrice,' then he divorced her once, she became separate (bain), her idda ended, then she spoke to Abu Amr, then he married her, then she spoke to Abu Yusuf, she is divorced thrice with the first one. And Zufar said: 'It does not occur.' And this has several aspects: either both conditions are found in marriage, then divorce occurs – this is apparent; or both are found outside marriage, then it does not occur; or the first is found in marriage and the second outside marriage, then also it does not occur because the penalty does not descend outside marriage; or the first is found outside marriage and the second in marriage – and this is the disputed issue of the book. [Zufar's evidence:] He considers the first analogous to the second because both are like one thing in the ruling of divorce. [Our evidence:] The validity of speech is based on the capacity of the speaker, except that marriage is stipulated at the time of suspension so that the penalty is likely to occur, based on istishab al-hal, so the oath is valid; and at the completion of the condition [marriage is required] so that the penalty descends, because it only descends in marriage. And between these two times is the state of the oath's remaining, so it is independent of the existence of marriage because its remaining is in its place, which is the dhimma. Translation: And if the husband said to his wife: 'If you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf, you are divorced thrice,' then he gave her one divorce, she became bain, her idda ended. Then she spoke to Abu Amr. Then he married her. Then she spoke to Abu Yusuf. So this woman is thrice-divorced along with the first one. And Imam Zufar said that three do not occur. And this issue has several forms: either both conditions are found in marriage – then divorce occurs, and this is apparent; or both are found outside marriage – then it does not occur; or the first is in marriage and the second outside marriage – then also it does not occur because the penalty does not descend outside marriage; or the first is outside marriage and the second in marriage – and this is the disputed issue of the book. Imam Zufar's evidence is that he analogizes the first to the second because both are like one thing in the ruling of divorce. And our evidence is that the correctness of speech is with the qualification of the speaker, except that marriage is stipulated at the time of suspension so that the penalty is likely to exist, due to istishab al-hal, so the oath is valid; and at the completion of the condition so that the penalty descends, because it only descends in marriage. And between these two is the state of the oath's remaining, so it is independent of the existence of marriage, because its remaining is in its place, which is the dhimma. Explanation of the issue: If the husband said to his wife: 'If you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf, you are divorced thrice,' then the husband gave her one divorce. So she became bain and her idda ended. Then the woman spoke to Abu Amr while she was not his wife. Then he married her. Then the woman spoke to Abu Yusuf while she was his wife. So in this case...
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute from Ashraf al-Hidayah. The issue is a conditional divorce suspended on speaking to two specific persons. The husband says: 'If you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf, you are divorced thrice.' He then gives one talaq (making her bain), her idda expires, she speaks to Abu Amr (outside marriage), then he remarries her, then she speaks to Abu Yusuf (within marriage). The Hanafi ruling (as per Abu Hanifa and his students) is that three talaqs occur in total: the first one given plus the three from the condition? Wait, the text says: 'She is divorced thrice with the first one' – meaning the condition triggers three talaqs, and the first one was already given, so total four? But the translation says she is 'thrice-divorced along with the first one' – i.e., the condition results in three talaqs that add to the first? Actually, careful: The text says: 'فهي طالق ثلاثاً مع الواحدة الأولى' – she is divorced thrice along with the first one. This likely means the condition triggers three talaqs, making her irrevocably divorced (total of one given + three from condition = four? But three talaqs are the maximum for a full divorce. In Hanafi law, if a man divorces his wife once, then remarries her, and then a condition triggers three talaqs, that would be a total of four? But three talaqs completely dissolve the marriage irrevocably. The text might mean that the condition itself yields a triple talaq (three divorces) and that, combined with the first, makes her definitively divorced. However, in the scenario, she was divorced once (bain), then remarried, then the condition triggered three talaqs, so she is divorced thrice from the second marriage. The text says she is 'divorced thrice with the first one' – perhaps the first divorce is separate. This requires careful reading. The immediate ruling: she becomes irrevocably divorced (three talaqs) as a result of the condition being fulfilled (speaking to Abu Yusuf while in marriage). Zufar's position: no talaq occurs because he considers the two speeches as a single condition; since one speech (to Abu Amr) occurred outside marriage, the entire condition is invalid. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the validity of the oath requires marriage at the time of suspension and at the time of fulfillment of the penalty; but the oath itself remains in force during the separation. Thus, the second speech (to Abu Yusuf) occurring in marriage triggers the full penalty of three talaqs. The text then enumerates all possible scenarios: both speeches in marriage → talaq occurs; both outside → no; first in, second out → no (penalty cannot descend outside marriage); first out, second in → disputed, with the Hanafi ruling that it does occur.

Key Terms
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspending the occurrence of divorce on a future condition (speaking to two persons).
جزاء (jaza'): The penalty/result of the condition – i.e., the divorce that is triggered.
یمین (yamin): Oath; here, the conditional divorce is treated as an oath (yamin) that remains binding.
ملک (milk): Ownership; here, the state of being married (nikah).
ذمہ (dhimma): The legal capacity/liability of a person; the oath resides in the dhimma.

A) Because the wife is still in idda.
B) Because the oath resides in the dhimma and is not dependent on ongoing marriage.
C) Because the husband intended to keep the oath active.
D) Because the first divorce was only one talaq.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a conditional divorce suspended on multiple acts remains binding even if some acts occur outside marriage, as long as the final act completing the condition occurs within marriage.

Conditional Divorce with Linked Conditions: Abu Hanifa vs. Imam Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional divorce with linked conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional divorce when one condition occurs outside marriage and the second within a subsequent marriage, and explain why the oath remains valid despite the gap in marriage.

Core Idea
An oath of divorce remains valid even if a condition occurs outside marriage, because the oath resides in the dhimma.

In Hanafi fiqh, conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) is treated as an oath. A common question arises when multiple conditions are linked by 'and': what happens if one condition occurs while the wife is not married, but the other occurs after remarriage? This lesson examines the case of a man who says, 'If you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf, you are thrice divorced,' and then divorces her once, she later speaks to Abu Amr while single, then remarries and speaks to Abu Yusuf. We will explore the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the dissenting view of Imam Zufar, learning how the Hanafi school relies on istishab al-hal and the concept of the oath's persistence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ikhtilaf
State the case: husband says conditional divorce with two conditions, then gives one divorce, first condition occurs outside marriage, second inside remarriage. The ikhtilaf: does the conditional divorce take effect?
2
State Zufar's position and his qiyas
Zufar says no divorce, because the two conditions are like one unit; since the first condition occurred without marriage, the whole conditional fails.
Zufar's analogy: just as the second condition requires marriage for divorce to occur, so does the first.
3
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Abu Hanifa says divorce does occur; the oath is valid based on speaker's capacity; marriage is required at ta'liq and at fulfillment, but the oath persists in the dhimma.
The Hanafi proof: validity of speech depends on eligibility of the speaker, not on continuous marriage.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response using istishab
The Hanafi use istishab al-hal to presume marriage continues at the time of ta'liq, making the consequence likely. The oath remains independent.
Istishab al-hal provides a presumption that the marriage state continues, making the consequence probable.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Practical difference: in this scenario, Zufar says no divorce, Abu Hanifa says three divorces (including the first). The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قال لها ان كلمت ابا عمرو وابا يوسف فانت طالق ثلاثا ثم طلقها واحدة فبانت وانقضت عدتها فكلمت ابا عمرو ثم تزوجها فكلمت ابا يوسف فهي طالق ثلاثاً مع الواحدة الاولى وقال زفر لا يقع وهذه على وجوه اما ان وجد الشرطان فى الملك فيقع الطلاق وهذا ظاهر او وجدا فى غير الملك فلا يقع او وجد الاول في الملك والثاني في غير الملك فلا يقع ايضا لان الجزاء لا ينزل في غير الملك فلا يقع او وجد الاول في غير الملك والثاني في الملك وهى مسالة الكتاب الخلافية له اعتبار الاول بالثاني اذهما فى حكم الطلاق كشيء واحد ولنا ان صحة الكلام باهلية المتكلم الا ان الملك يشترط حالة التعليق ليصير الجزاء غالب الوجود لاستصحاب الحال فيصح اليمين وعند تمام الشرط لينزل الجزاء لانه لا ينزل الا فى الملك و فيما بين ذلك الحال حال بقاء اليمين فيستغنى عن قيام الملك اذ بقاؤه بمحله وهو الذمة
And if he said to her: 'If you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf, then you are thrice divorced.' Then he gave her one divorce, so she became bain (irrevocably divorced) and her iddah ended. Then she spoke to Abu Amr, then he married her, then she spoke to Abu Yusuf. Then she is thrice divorced along with the first one. And Zufar said: 'It does not occur.' And this [case] has aspects: if both conditions occur in marriage, the divorce occurs—this is apparent. If both occur outside marriage, it does not occur. If the first occurs in marriage and the second outside marriage, it also does not occur because the consequence does not descend outside marriage, so it does not occur. Or if the first occurs outside marriage and the second in marriage—and this is the disputed case of the book. His [Zufar's] reasoning is that the first is analogized to the second, because both are like a single thing in the ruling of divorce. And our proof is that the validity of speech depends on the eligibility of the speaker, except that marriage is stipulated at the time of suspension (ta'liq) so that the consequence becomes likely to occur due to istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity), thus the oath becomes valid. And at the completion of the condition, marriage is required for the consequence to descend, because it only descends in marriage. And in between these two states is the state of the oath remaining. He is independent of the existence of marriage because its remaining is in its place, which is the dhimma (legal responsibility).
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya explains a complex case of conditional divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) involving two conditions linked by 'and' (waw). The husband says to his wife: 'If you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf, you are thrice divorced.' He then gives her one divorce, making her bain (irrevocable divorce). After her iddah ends, she speaks to Abu Amr while not married. Later, he remarries her, and she speaks to Abu Yusuf while married. The question is whether the conditional divorce (three divorces) takes effect. According to Abu Hanifa (and the Sahibayn), she becomes thrice divorced, taking into account the first divorce as well. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that since the first condition (speaking to Abu Amr) occurred outside marriage, the entire conditional is ineffective because the conditions are like a single unit. He uses qiyas (analogy): just as the second condition requires marriage for the divorce to occur, so does the first. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the validity of the oath (yamin) and the requirement of marriage for the consequence (jaza') to descend. The oath is valid based on the speaker's capacity (ahliyyat al-mutakallim). Marriage is stipulated at the time of ta'liq to make the consequence likely to occur (ghalib al-wujud) due to istishab al-hal (presumption that the current state continues). At the time the condition is fulfilled, marriage is necessary for the consequence to actually descend, because divorce can only occur in marriage. However, in the intermediate period between ta'liq and fulfillment, the oath remains in effect independent of marriage, because its place (mahal) is the dhimma (legal responsibility) which always exists. Thus, the first condition occurring outside marriage does not invalidate the conditional. The passage also enumerates four possible scenarios: (1) both conditions in marriage: divorce occurs; (2) both outside: no divorce; (3) first in marriage, second outside: no divorce; (4) first outside, second in marriage: this is the disputed case. The Hanafi view is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position).

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): The suspension of a legal consequence (here talaq) upon the occurrence of a future condition.
جزاء (jaza'): The consequence that occurs upon fulfillment of the condition, here talaq.
يمين (yamin): An oath; here a conditional divorce considered as a yamin.
ملک (milk): Marriage; the legal bond that makes the spouse a wife.
استصحاب (istishab): Presumption of continuity of a state until proven otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case discussed, what is the Hanafi ruling when the first condition (speaking to Abu Amr) occurs outside marriage and the second (speaking to Abu Yusuf) occurs within a subsequent marriage?
A) No divorce occurs because both conditions are like a single unit.
B) Three divorces occur, combining with the first divorce.
C) Only one divorce occurs.
D) The conditional divorce is invalid due to the absence of marriage at the first condition.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a conditional divorce oath persists independently of marriage; only the occurrence of the condition and the descent of the consequence require marriage at specific times.

Four Scenarios for Conditional Divorce with Two Conditions
Classifies four scenarios for conditional divorce based on timing of marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the four scenarios of conditional divorce with two conditions and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar regarding the fourth scenario.

Core Idea
The validity of a conditional oath depends on the speaker's eligibility, not on marriage at each condition.

Conditional divorce (talīq al-talāq) involves suspending divorce on the occurrence of one or more conditions. When two conditions are stipulated, the timing of their occurrence relative to the marriage contract becomes critical. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah classifies four possible scenarios and examines a disagreement within the Hanafi school between Imam Abu Hanifa (and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Zufar. The core question: if the first condition occurs before marriage and the second after, does divorce take effect? Understanding this dispute requires careful attention to the basis of oath validity and the role of marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
The text lists four possibilities based on whether each condition occurs during marriage (milkiyyah) or outside (ghayr milk). State each.
The first two have consensus; the third is also agreed upon; only the fourth is disputed.
2
Determine the consensus points
Both conditions during marriage: divorce occurs. Both outside: no divorce. First during, second outside: no divorce because the consequence cannot descend outside marriage.
The reasoning for the third scenario is that the jaza' (divorce) must occur in milk.
3
Focus on the disputed fourth scenario
Fourth scenario: first condition outside marriage, second during marriage. Imam Zufar argues that the conditional divorce is void; the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that divorce occurs upon fulfillment of the second condition.
This is the crux of the ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze Imam Zufar's analogy
Zufar draws qiyas: just as the second condition requires marriage for divorce to occur, so must the first. Since the first occurred outside marriage, the entire conditional divorce is invalid.
Zufar treats the two conditions as a single unit; each condition requires marriage at its time of occurrence.
5
Understand the Hanafi response
The majority argue that oath validity depends on the speaker's eligibility (adult, sane) and the oath's place is his conscience, not marriage. Marriage is required only at the time of suspension to make the consequence likely (istishab al-hal). The oath continues even if marriage temporarily ends; only the descent of divorce requires current marriage.
Istishab presumes continuation of marriage at the time of suspension, but not throughout the interval.

پہلی ایک کے ساتھ مل کر تین طلاقوں کے ساتھ مطلقہ ہوگی اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ واقع نہیں ہوں گی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کی چند صورتیں ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ دونوں شرطیں ملک میں پائی جائیں۔ اس صورت میں بالا تفاق طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ شر ط طلاق ملک میں پائی گئی دوم یہ کہ دونوں شرطیں غیر ملک میں پائی جائیں اس صورت میں بالا تفاق طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی سوم یہ کہ شرط اول ملک میں اور شرط ثانی غیر ملک میں پائی جائے اس صورت میں بھی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ کہ جزاء یعنی طلاق غیر ملک میں نہیں اترتی لہذا طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ چہارم یہ کہ شرط اول غیر ملک میں اور شرط ثانی ملک میں پائی جائے۔ یہ مسئلہ کتاب ہے جو ہمارے اور امام زفر کے مابین مختلف فیہ ہے۔
مسلم کتاب میں امام زفر کی دلیل شرط اول کا شرط ثانی پر قیاس ہے اس کے دو مطلب ہیں ایک یہ کہ شرط ثانی اگر غیر ملک میں پائی جائے تو جزاء یعنی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی۔ اسی طرح جب شرط اول غیر ملک میں پائی جائے تو طلاق واقع نہ ہونی چاہئے۔ دوسرا مطلب اول کو ثانی پر قیاس کرنے کا یہ ہے کہ جس طرح شرط ثانی کے وقت وقوع طلاق کیلئے ملک شرط ہے ایسے ہی شرط اول کے پائے جانے کے وقت بھی وقوع طلاق کیلئے ملک شرط ہونی چاہئے۔ اسلئے کہ یہ دونوں شرطیں طلاق کے حکم میں ( یعنی طلاق ان دونوں کے ساتھ واقع ہو گی )۔ شرط واحد کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ اور اگر شرط واحد ہوتی تو بغیر ملک کے طلاق واقع نہ ہوتی۔ پس ایسے ہی یہاں بھی بغیر ملک کے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ے کہ کلام مین کا صیح ہونا مشکل کی لیاقت اور اہلیت سے ہے۔ اور متکلم عاقل بالغ ہونے کی وجہ سے اہلیت بیبین کا حامل ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کلام یمین درست ہو گیا اور اس بیبین کامل حالف کا ذمہ ہے۔
الا ان الملک سے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ جب صحت کلام کیلئے اہلیت متکلم کافی اور محل یمین حالف کا ذمہ ہے تو پھر تعلیق کے وقت ملک کی شرط کیوں لگائی گئی ؟ جواب یہ ہے کہ تعلیق کے وقت ملک کی شرط اسلئے لگائی ہے تا کہ جزاء غالب الوجود ہو سکے۔ دلیل استصحاب حال کی وجہ سے ۔ استصحاب حال کہتے ہیں ابقاء ما كان على ما كان لعدم الدليل المزيل يعني دليل مزیل کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے جو چیز جیسی تھی اس کو ویسی ہی باقی رکھنا۔ حاصل یہ کہ جب تعلیق کے وقت ملک موجود ہے تو غالب گمان یہی ہے کہ وجود شرط کے وقت تک موجود رہے گی۔ استصحاب حال کی وجہ سے اگر چہ ملک کے زائل ہونے کا اسوقت بھی ہے بہر حال جب جزاء غالب الوجود ہے تو سیمین درست ہو گئی ۔ اور تمام شرط کے وقت بقاء ملک کی شرط اسلئے لگائی گئی ہے تا کہ جزاء اتر سکے۔ یعنی متحقق ہو سکے۔ کیونکہ وجود جزاء ملک میں متحقق ہوسکتا ہے نہ کہ غیر ملک میں۔ اور ان دو حالتوں کے درمیان بقاء یمین کی حالت ہے۔ اور بقاء یمین ملک کی محتاج نہیں ہوتی ۔ کیونکہ یمین کی بقاء اسکے محل کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے اور محل حالف کا ذمہ ہے۔ جو ہر وقت موجود ہے۔ اسلئے درمیان کے زمانہ میں ملک کا ہونا لازم قرار نہیں دیا گیا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
(The beginning of this passage is missing context: it states that the woman would be divorced with three divorces when the first condition is combined with the second, and Imam Zufar said they would not occur.) The author of Al-Hidayah says that this issue has several scenarios: First, both conditions occur during marriage. In this case, by consensus, divorce occurs because the condition of divorce occurred during marriage. Second, both conditions occur outside marriage. In this case, by consensus, divorce does not occur. Third, the first condition occurs during marriage and the second outside marriage. In this case also divorce does not occur. The proof: the consequence (i.e., divorce) does not descend outside marriage, so divorce does not occur. Fourth, the first condition occurs outside marriage and the second during marriage. This is the issue under discussion, which is disputed between us and Imam Zufar. In the Musallam book, Imam Zufar's proof is an analogy of the first condition to the second. This has two meanings: one, if the second condition occurs outside marriage, then the consequence (divorce) does not occur. Similarly, when the first condition occurs outside marriage, divorce should not occur. The second meaning of analogizing the first to the second is that just as at the time of the second condition, marriage is a condition for the occurrence of divorce, similarly at the time of the occurrence of the first condition, marriage should be a condition for the occurrence of divorce, because these two conditions are like a single condition in the ruling of divorce (i.e., divorce occurs with both of them). And if it were a single condition, divorce would not occur without marriage. So similarly here, divorce will not occur without marriage. Our proof is that the correctness of speech is due to the capability and eligibility of the speaker. And because the speaker is an adult sane person, he possesses the eligibility for oath. Therefore, the oath speech is valid, and the liability of the oath is on the conscience of the swearer. The phrase 'illa an al-milk' is an answer to a presumed question. The question: When the eligibility of the speaker is sufficient for the validity of speech and the place of the oath is the conscience of the swearer, then why is marriage made a condition at the time of suspension? The answer: Marriage is made a condition at the time of suspension so that the consequence may be likely to occur. The proof is istishab al-hal: preserving what was as it was due to the absence of an evidence that removes it. The summary: When marriage exists at the time of suspension, the dominant presumption is that it will continue until the condition occurs, due to istishab, even though there is also a possibility of marriage ending. Nevertheless, when the consequence is likely to occur, the oath is valid. And the condition of the continuation of marriage at the time of the fulfillment of all conditions is so that the consequence may descend (i.e., materialize), because the existence of the consequence can only materialize in marriage, not outside marriage. And between these two states is the state of the continuation of the oath. The continuation of the oath does not require marriage, because the oath continues with its place, and the place is the conscience of the swearer, which exists at all times. Therefore, the existence of marriage during the intervening period is not deemed necessary. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on Al-Hidayah, discusses the ruling of a conditional divorce where two conditions are stipulated. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa (and his followers) and Imam Zufar. The author first states that there are four scenarios based on whether the conditions occur during marriage (milkiyyah) or outside it. In the first two scenarios, there is consensus: divorce occurs if both conditions occur during marriage, and does not occur if both occur outside marriage. In the third scenario (first condition during marriage, second outside), divorce does not occur because the consequence (divorce) cannot descend outside marriage. The disputed fourth scenario is when the first condition occurs outside marriage (e.g., before marriage) and the second during marriage. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that divorce occurs upon fulfillment of the second condition because the oath was validly made during marriage, and the continuation of marriage is not required between conditions. Imam Zufar argues by analogy that just as the second condition requires marriage for divorce to occur, so does the first, and since the first occurred outside marriage, the conditional divorce is void. The Hanafi response is that the validity of the oath depends on the eligibility of the speaker (being adult and sane) and the place of the oath is his conscience, not the marriage. The requirement of marriage at the time of suspension is only to make the consequence likely to occur (ghalib al-wujud), based on istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity). The marriage is not required for the continuation of the oath itself. Thus, if the second condition occurs during marriage, divorce takes effect.

Key Terms
ملک (milk): In this passage, milk refers to the existence of a valid marriage (nikah) at the time a condition is fulfilled.
جزاء (jaza'): The consequence of the condition, i.e., the divorce itself.
استصحاب حال (istishab al-hal): The legal presumption that a state continues unchanged in the absence of evidence to the contrary.
یمین (yamin): An oath, here referring to the conditional divorce statement (e.g., 'if you enter the house, you are divorced').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling when a husband says during marriage, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced thrice,' and the wife enters the house after they have divorced (i.e., after two divorces) and then remarried and returned? (The passage specifically discusses the fourth scenario: first condition outside marriage, second inside.)
A) No divorce occurs because the first condition was not during marriage.
B) Divorce occurs because the second condition occurred during marriage.
C) The conditional divorce is void because the first condition was invalid.
D) Only one divorce occurs because the first condition partially fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
In a conditional divorce with two conditions, the occurrence of the first condition outside marriage does not invalidate the oath; divorce takes effect if the second condition occurs during marriage.
