If a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced with three [divorces] except one', then two divorces occur. And if he says 'You are divorced with three except two', then one divorce occurs. And if he said 'you are divorced with three except one', she is divorced with two; and if he said 'you are divorced with three except two', she is divorced with one. The principle is that the exception is speaking with the remainder after the exception, this is correct. Its meaning is that he speaks with the excepted-from, for there is no difference between one's saying 'I have a dirham on so-and-so' and saying 'I have ten dirhams except nine'. So it is valid to except part from the whole, because speaking with the part remains after it. And it is not valid to except the whole, because nothing remains after it for him to speak with and direct the word to it. The exception is only valid if it is connected to the original statement, as we mentioned before. And when this is established, in the first chapter the excepted-from is two, so two occur; and in the second it is one, so one occurs. And if he said 'except three', three occur, because it is an exception of the whole from the whole, so the exception is not valid. And Allah knows best. Commentary: The issue is that if someone says to his wife 'You are divorced with three except one', then two occur; and if he says 'You are divorced with three except two', one occurs. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned two examples indicating that the exception is small and...
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage discusses numerical exceptions in divorce declarations. The primary ruling: if a husband says 'You are divorced with three except one', then two divorces occur; if 'except two', then one divorce occurs. The underlying principle (asl) is that an exception is valid only when it leaves something remaining from the original number. Exception of part from a whole is valid because after the exception, the speaker is effectively speaking about the remainder. Exception of the whole (e.g., 'three except three') is invalid because nothing remains; thus the original statement stands unchanged, and three divorces occur. The passage uses an analogy: saying 'I have ten dirhams except nine' is the same as saying 'I have one dirham' — the exception effectively states the remainder. The author then applies this to talaq: if the number is three and except one, the excepted-from (mustathna minhu) is two, so two divorces occur. If except two, the excepted-from is one. If except three, the exception is of the whole, so it is invalid and three divorces occur. The passage emphasizes that the exception must be connected to the original statement, as previously established. This lesson is a straightforward application of linguistic rules to divorce counts.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): An exception that excludes part of a number from the whole statement.
مستثنیٰ منہ (mustathna minhu): The remainder after the exception is taken out; e.g., in 'three except one', the excepted-from is two.
مستثنیٰ (mustathna): The part that is excepted, e.g., 'one' in 'except one'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says to his wife: 'You are divorced with three except three'. How many divorces occur according to the Hanafi school?
A) None, because the exception voids the entire statement.
B) One, because exception of the whole is reduced to one.
C) Three, because the exception of the whole is invalid and the original number stands.
D) Two, because three minus three equals zero but the minimum is one.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a numerical exception in divorce is valid only if it leaves a remainder; otherwise the original count stands.

Effect of Wife's Death Before Completion of Istithna in Talaq
Ruling on divorce occurrence when wife dies before husband completes istithna

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on istithna when death interrupts the divorce pronouncement and distinguish between the cases where the wife dies before or after the exception.

Core Idea
A divorce pronouncement with incomplete istithna is void if the wife dies before the exception is spoken.

This lesson examines a nuanced situation in Hanafi divorce law: what happens when the wife dies after the husband begins a divorce pronouncement but before he completes the exception phrase 'Insha Allah'. The ruling turns on whether the exception was connected to the pronouncement and how death affects the legal validity of the utterance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Husband says 'anti taliq... Insha Allah', but wife dies before he says 'Insha Allah'. The ruling: divorce does not occur.
The act is an incomplete pronouncement of divorce with an exception.
2
Understand the basis
The istithna (exception) removes the utterance from being a definitive pronouncement (ijab). Once the ijab is voided, the legal effect (divorce) is also void.
The proof given is that the exception causes the speech to leave the category of ijab.
3
Consider the objection and response
Objection: Since the ijab occurred during the wife's life, the later exception should be invalid, so the ijab should stand. Response: Death contradicts the pronouncer (husband), not the invalidator. Both death and istithna are invalidators; no conflict.
Key distinction: the wife's death invalidates the utterance, not the exception.
4
Contrast with husband's death
If the husband dies after saying 'anti taliq' but before 'Insha Allah', the divorce does occur because the exception was not connected to the pronouncement at the time of death.
The outcome depends on who dies and the timing of the exception relative to the completion of the pronouncement.

کتاب الطلاق
اور ایسے ہی اگر عورت شوہر کے لفظ ان شاء اللہ کہنے سے پہلے مرگئی تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ دلیل یہ کہ استثناء کی وجہ سے کلام ایجاب ہونے سے نکل گیا۔ پس جب ایجاب باطل ہو گیا تو حکم بھی باطل ہو گیا۔
والموت ينافی الموجب سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ ایجاب یعنی انت طالق عورت کی حیات میں پایا گیا۔اور استثناء اس کے بعد پایا گیا تو عدم محل کی وجہ سے استثناء باطل ہو گیا۔ اور جب استثناء باطل ہو گیا تو ایجاب صحیح ہو گیا۔ لہذا طلاق واقع ہونی چاہئے ۔ جواب موت موجب کے منافی ہوتی ہے۔ نہ کہ مبطل کے۔ چنانچہ انت طالق کا تلفظ پورا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے اگر عورت مر گئی تو ایجاب باطل ہو جائیگا۔ اور مبطل یعنی استثناء یا شرط موت سے باطل نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ موت بھی منبطل ہے اور استثناء بھی مبطل اور مبطل مبطل کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر انت طالق کہنے کے بعد اور انشاء اللہ کہنے سے پہلے شوہر کا وصال ہو گیا تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں انت طالق کے ساتھ استثناء متصل نہیں ہوا۔
And similarly, if the woman died before the husband said 'Insha Allah', then divorce does not occur. The proof is that due to the istithna, the speech left being a definite pronouncement (ijab). When the ijab became void, the ruling also became void. 'And death contradicts the pronouncer' is the answer to an objection. The objection is: the ijab, i.e., 'anti taliq', occurred during the wife's life, and the istithna occurred after, so due to the absence of place (the wife's life), the istithna becomes void. When the istithna is void, the ijab becomes valid. Therefore, divorce should occur. The answer: death contradicts the pronouncer, not the invalidator. Thus, if the woman dies before the pronunciation of 'anti taliq' is complete, the ijab becomes void. But the invalidator, i.e., the istithna or condition, is not voided by death because death is also an invalidator and istithna is also an invalidator, and there is no contradiction between an invalidator and an invalidator. On the contrary, if the husband passed away after saying 'anti taliq' and before saying 'Insha Allah', then divorce would occur because in that case the istithna was not connected to 'anti taliq'.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school on the effect of istithna (exception) in talaq when interrupted by death. The text first states the ruling: if the wife dies before the husband completes the phrase 'Insha Allah' as an exception to the divorce pronouncement, the divorce does not take effect. The proof is that the exception removes the speech from being a definitive pronouncement (ijab); once the ijab is invalidated, its legal effect also ceases. The passage then addresses a potential objection: since the ijab ('anti taliq') occurred while the wife was alive, and the exception came after her death, the exception should be invalid due to the absence of a valid subject, thus the ijab should stand and divorce should occur. The author responds by explaining that death contradicts the pronouncer (the husband), not the invalidator. If the wife dies before the utterance 'anti taliq' is complete, the ijab itself is voided. Death and the istithna are both invalidators (mubtil), and there is no contradiction between two invalidators; thus the istithna remains valid and prevents the divorce. However, if the husband dies after saying 'anti taliq' but before saying 'Insha Allah', divorce does occur because the istithna was not connected to the pronouncement, so the ijab is complete. This distinction reflects the Hanafi principle that istithna must be connected to the original statement to be effective.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā’): An exception or exclusion made by the speaker in a pronouncement, e.g., 'You are divorced except if Allah wills'.
ایجاب (ījāb): The pronouncement or expression that establishes a legal obligation or effect, such as saying 'anti taliq'.
مبطل (mubṭil): That which invalidates or nullifies a legal act, such as death or an invalid exception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the wife dies before the husband completes 'Insha Allah' in a divorce pronouncement, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Divorce occurs because the pronouncement was made.
B) Divorce does not occur because the istithna invalidates the pronouncement.
C) Divorce is suspended pending resurrection.
D) Divorce occurs only if the husband intended it.

Key Takeaway
The death of the wife before the completion of an istithna in a divorce pronouncement invalidates the pronouncement because the exception is an invalidator that conflicts with the death of the pronouncer, preventing the divorce from taking effect.

Istithna in Triple Divorce: Exception Reduces the Count
Explaining the ruling and principle of istithna in triple divorce pronouncements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istithna in triple divorce and apply the principle of valid exception to determine the number of divorces that occur.

Core Idea
A valid exception reduces the divorces; an exception of the whole is void.

When a husband pronounces three divorces subject to an exception, the number of divorces that actually occur depends on the validity of the exception. The Hanafi school, following the linguistic principle that an exception leaves a remainder, determines the outcome by simple subtraction. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the principle, and the proof by way of analogy to debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a husband saying to his wife a phrase like 'you are divorced three except one'. The ruling is that two divorces occur. Similarly, 'except two' yields one divorce. 'Except three' yields three divorces because the exception is invalid.
The exception must leave at least one remaining item to be valid.
2
Locate the underlying principle (asl)
The principle is that istithna is speaking of what remains after the exception. It is valid only when part of the whole remains, and the exception is connected to the original statement.
This principle is derived from linguistic usage and applied by qiyas.
3
Follow the qiyas (analogy) proof
The text analogizes to debt: saying 'I owe ten dirhams except nine' is equivalent to saying 'I owe one dirham'. Thus, excepting a part from the whole reduces the spoken amount to the remainder. In divorce, excepting one from three leaves two, so two divorces occur.
The illa is that the exception reduces the quantity to the remainder.
4
Analyze the invalid exception
If the husband says 'except three', it is an exception of the whole from the whole. Nothing remains, so the exception is invalid and all three divorces occur.
This shows the condition that a valid exception must leave at least one remaining item.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some scholars (e.g., a French scholar mentioned in the commentary) do not permit a large exception from a small total. The Hanafi school permits it as long as a remainder exists.
This lesson follows the Hanafi position.

If a husband says to his wife 'you are divorced three except one', then two divorces occur; if he says 'you are divorced three except two', then one divorce occurs. And if he says 'you are divorced three except one', she is divorced by two; and if he says 'you are divorced three except two', she is divorced by one. The principle is that istithna is speaking of what remains after the exception; that is correct. Its meaning is that he speaks of the excepted-from portion. Because there is no difference between a person's statement 'I owe so-and-so one dirham' and his statement 'ten dirhams except nine'. Thus, excepting a part from the whole is valid because after the exception, speech about the part remains. Excepting the whole from the whole is not valid because nothing remains after it such that he would be speaking of it and turning the word towards it. Istithna is only valid when it is connected to the original statement, as we mentioned before. And when this is established, then in the first case the excepted-from is two, so they occur; in the second case it is one, so one occurs. And if he says 'except three', three occur because it is excepting the whole from the whole, so the exception is not valid. And Allah knows best. Translation: And if he said 'you are divorced' with three divorces except one, she becomes divorced with two divorces. And if he said 'you are divorced' with three divorces except two, she becomes divorced with one. And the rule is that istithna is speaking of the amount that remains after the exception; that is correct. Its meaning is that he spoke of the excepted-from portion. Because there is no difference between the two statements: 'I owe so-and-so one dirham' and 'I owe ten dirhams except nine'. So excepting a part from the whole is valid because after the exception, speech about the part remains. And excepting the whole from the whole is not valid because after that exception nothing remains such that he would be speaking of it and turning the word towards it. And istithna is valid only when connected to the original statement, as we mentioned before. And when this is established, then in the first case the excepted-from is two, so they occur; in the second case it is one, so one occurs. And if he said 'except three', three occur because it is excepting the whole from the whole, so the exception is not valid. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The issue is that if someone said to his wife 'you are divorced three except one', then in this case two occur. And if he said 'you are divorced three except two', then one occurs. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, pointed out by mentioning these two examples that both small and large exceptions are permissible, even though the French [scholar?] did not permit it. The principle of istithna is that it is the regulation of what remains after the exception. In short, speaking of the amount that remains from the excepted-from is called istithna. Hence, a person's statement 'so-and-so owes me one dirham' and his statement 'so-and-so owes me ten dirhams except nine'—there is no difference between these two statements. So it is concluded that excepting a part from the whole is correct, and excepting the whole from the whole is not correct, because after excepting the whole, nothing remains for which he can be called speaking of it. And for the validity of istithna, it is also necessary that the istithna be connected to the original statement. In any case, when this principle is established, then in the first scenario the remaining amount from the excepted-from is two, so two divorces occur. And in the second scenario, the amount remaining after the exception is one, so one divorce occurs. And if the husband said 'you are divorced three except three', then in this case the exception is invalid, and three divorces occur, because it is excepting the whole from the whole, and excepting the whole is not correct, because after the exception nothing remains which can be called his speech. And Allah, the Glorified and Exalted, knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the effect of istithna (exception) in the pronouncement of triple divorce. The text begins by stating the ruling: if a husband says 'you are divorced three times except one', two divorces occur; if he says 'except two', one divorce occurs. It then provides the underlying principle (asl): istithna is valid only when something remains after the exception, and it must be connected to the original statement. The proof is given through an analogy (qiyas) with financial debt: saying 'I owe ten dirhams except nine' is equivalent to saying 'I owe one dirham', because the exception reduces the whole to the remainder. Similarly, in divorce, the exception reduces the number of divorces to the remaining count. The text also addresses the case where the husband says 'except three' (i.e., excepting all three): the exception is invalid because it is an exception of the whole from the whole, leaving no remainder, so three divorces occur. The commentary emphasizes that both small and large exceptions are permissible in the Hanafi school, contrary to the view of some scholars. The practical application is clear: the number of divorces is determined by subtracting the exception from the total.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā’): An exception in speech that removes part of the whole from the ruling.
مستثنى منه (mustathnā minhu): The quantity from which the exception is made, e.g., three in 'three except one'.
مستثنى (mustathnā): The quantity that is excepted, e.g., one in 'three except one'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'anti taliq thalathan illa thalathan' (you are divorced three except three), how many divorces occur according to the Hanafi school?
A) None, because the exception invalidates all.
B) One, because the exception leaves nothing.
C) Three, because the exception is invalid.
D) Two, because the exception reduces by one.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a valid istithna reduces the number of divorces by the excepted amount, but an exception of the whole is void and all original divorces occur.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Validity of Istithna (Exception) in Divorce Pronouncements
Explains the validity of exception in divorce and its effect on number of divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid istithna in divorce and apply them to determine the number of divorces that occur.

Core Idea
An exception in divorce is valid only if it leaves some number remaining and is uttered without interruption.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi ruling on using exceptions (istithna) in divorce pronouncements. The exception must meet two conditions: it must be connected (ittisal) to the original statement, and it must leave some part of the number remaining. If these conditions are violated—such as exception of the whole or disconnection—the exception is invalid and the full number of divorces takes effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is pronouncing divorce with an exception. The ruling is that the exception is valid if it meets the conditions; otherwise, the divorce stands as if no exception was made.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is the linguistic principle: exception is speech about what remains after the exception. This is a linguistic certainty.
The dalil is 'aqli (rational) based on language usage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The principle shows that exception of the whole (e.g., three except three) is meaningless because nothing remains to be spoken about; thus the exception is invalid.
This is the key to understanding the invalidity of istithna al-kull.
4
Note the condition of ittisal
The exception must be connected to the original statement without interruption. Death or a significant break invalidates the connection.
Husband's death after declaration but before exception: divorce occurs because ittisal is broken. Wife's death before completion: no divorce.
5
Apply to numeric examples
Apply the rule: 'three except one' leaves two, so two divorces occur; 'three except two' leaves one; 'three except three' is invalid, so three occur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ينافی الموجب سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ ایجاب یعنی انت طالق عورت کی حیات میں پایا گیا۔اور استثناء اس کے بعد پایا گیا تو عدم محل کی وجہ سے استثناء باطل ہو گیا۔ اور جب استثناء باطل ہو گیا تو ایجاب صحیح ہو گیا۔ لہذا طلاق واقع ہوئی چاہئے ۔ جواب موت موجب کے منافی ہوتی ہے۔ نہ کہ مبطل کے۔ چنانچہ انت طالق کا تلفظ پورا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے اگر عورت مر گئی تو ایجاب باطل ہو جائیگا۔ اور مبطل یعنی استثناء یا شرط موت سے باطل نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ موت بھی مبطل ہے اور استثناء بھی مبطل اور مبطل مبطل کے درمیان کوئی منافات نہیں ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر انت طالق کہنے کے بعد اور انشاء اللہ کہنے سے پہلے شوہر کا وصال ہو گیا تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں انت طالق کے ساتھ استثناء متصل نہیں ہوا۔ شوہر نے منکوحہ سے کہا انت طالق ثلاثا الا واحدة تو دو طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی اور اگر کہا انت طالق ثلاثا الا ثنتین تو ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی وان قال انت طالق ثلثا الاواحدة طلقت ثنتين وان قال انت طالق ثلثا الاثنتين طلقت واحدة والاصل آن الاستثناء تكلم بالحاصل بعد الثنيا هو الصحيح ومعناه انه تكلم بالمستثنى منه اذلافرق بين قول القائل لفلان على درهم وبين قوله عشرة الاتسعة فيصح استثناء البعض من الجملة لانه يبقى التكلم بالبعض بعده ولا يصح استثناء الكل لانه لا يبقى بعده شيء ليصير متكلمابه وصارفا للفظ اليه وانما يصح الاستثناء اذا كان موصولا به كما ذكرنا من قبل واذا ثبت هذا ففى الفصل الأول المستثنى منه ثنتان فيقعان وفى الثانى واحدة فيقع واحدة ولو قال الا ثلثا يقع الثلث لانه استثناء الكل من الكل فلم يصح الاستثناء والله اعلم ترجمہ اور اگر کہا تو طالقہ بہ طلاق ہے مگر ایک تو دو طلاقوں کے ساتھ طالقہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر کہا تو طالقہ بسہ طلاق ہے۔ سوائے دو کے۔ تو ایک کے ساتھ مطلقہ ہوگی۔ اور ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ استثناء اس مقدار کا تکلم کرنا ہے جو استثناء کے بعد حاصل ہوئی۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔ اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ باقی مستثنی منہ کے ساتھ کلام کیا۔ اسلئے کہ کوئی فرق نہیں۔ ان دو قولوں کے درمیان کہ فلان کیلئے مجھ پر ایک درہم ہے اور دس درہم ہیں سوائے نو کے ۔ تو کل سے بعض کا استثناء کرنا صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ استثناء کے بعد بعض کا تکلم باقی رہے گا۔ اور کل کا استثناء کرنا کل سے صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس استثناء کے بعد کچھ باقی نہیں رہا۔ تا کہ اس کے ساتھ تکلم کرنے والا ہو جائے اور لفظ کو اس کی طرف پھیرنے والا ۔ اور اتنا صحیح ہوگا جبکہ اصل کلام کے ساتھ متصل ہو۔ جیسا کہ ہم نے سابق میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور جب یہ ثابت ہو گیا تو پہلے مسلہ میں مستقلی من دو ہیں۔ سو واقع ہوں گی اور دوسرے مسئلہ میں ایک ہے۔ پس وہ ایک واقع ہوگی ۔ اور اگر کہا الا ثلاثا تو تین واقع ہوں گی۔ کیونکہ یہ کل کا استثناء کل سے ہے۔ لہذا استثناء بیچ نہیں ہوا۔ اور اللہ زیادہ واقف ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا انت طالق ثلاثاً الا واحدة تو اس صورت میں دو واقع ہوں گی ۔ اور اگر انت طالق ثلاثاً الاثنتین کہا تو ایک واقع ہوگی۔ مصنف علیہ الرحمہ نے دو مثالیں ذکر فرما کر اس جانب اشارہ کیا ہے کہ استثنا قلیل و کثیر دونوں کا جائز ہے اگر چہ فرا نحوی نے اس کی اجازت نہیں دی ہے۔ استثناء کی اصل یہ ہے کہ استثناء کرنے کے بعد جو مقدار باقی رہی اس کا تکلم کرنا استثناء ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ مستثنی منہ کی جو مقدار باقی رہ گئی اس کا تکلم کرنا استثناء کہلائے گا۔ لہذا ایک آدمی کا قول کہ فلاں کا مجھ پر ایک درہم ہے اور اس کا قول کہ فلاں کے مجھ پر دس درہم ہیں نو کے علاوہ ان دونوں اقوال میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ پس حاصل یہ نکلا کہ کل سے بعض کا استثناء کرنا درست ہے۔ اور کل کا کل سے استثناء درست نہیں۔ کیونکہ کل کا استثناء کرنے کے بعد کچھ باقی نہیں رہے گا جس کے ساتھ تکلم کرنے والا ہو۔ اور استثناء کی صحت کیلئے یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ استثناء اصل کلام کے ساتھ متصل ہو۔ بہر حال جب یہ اصول ثابت ہو گیا تو پہلی صورت میں مستنئی منہ سے باقی ماندہ مقدار دو ہیں ۔ لہذا دو طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ اور دوسری صورت میں استثناء کے بعد باقی ماندہ ایک ہے۔ لہذا ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ اور اگر شوہر نے کہا است طالق ثلاثاً الا ثلاثاً تو اس صورت میں استثناء باطل ہو گا۔ اور تین طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی ۔ کیونکہ یہ کل کا استثناء کل سے ہے۔ اور کل کا استثناء کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ استثناء کرنے کے بعد کوئی چیز باقی نہیں رہنی جس کے ساتھ اس کو تکلم کرنے والا کہا جائے۔ والله سبحانه و تعالى اعلم بالصواب
If a wife dies before her husband says 'in sha Allah', divorce does not occur. The proof is that due to the exception, the statement leaves being an ijab (declaration). So when the ijab becomes invalid, the ruling also becomes invalid. 'And death contradicts the one making ijab' is the answer to a question. The question is: The ijab, i.e., 'anti taliq', occurred during the wife's lifetime, and the exception occurred after it, so due to lack of subject (mahal), the exception becomes invalid. And when the exception becomes invalid, the ijab becomes valid, so divorce should occur. The answer: Death contradicts the one making ijab, not that which nullifies (mubtil). Thus, if the wife dies before completing the utterance of 'anti taliq', the ijab becomes invalid. The mubtil (exception or condition) is not invalidated by death because death is also a mubtil and exception is also a mubtil, and there is no contradiction between two mubtils. Conversely, if the husband dies after saying 'anti taliq' and before saying 'in sha Allah', divorce occurs because in this case the exception is not connected to 'anti taliq'. A man said to his wife: 'You are divorced three except one' — two divorces occur. If he said: 'You are divorced three except two' — one divorce occurs. The principle is: Exception is speech concerning what remains after making the exception; this is correct. Its meaning is that he speaks about the remainder of the excepted matter. There is no difference between one saying: 'I owe so-and-so one dirham' and saying 'ten dirhams except nine'. So exception of part from the whole is valid because speech about part remains after it. Exception of the whole is invalid because nothing remains after it to be spoken of and direct the wording to it. Exception is only valid when connected [to the original statement] as we mentioned earlier. When this is established, in the first case the excepted-from (mustathna minhu) is two, so two occur. In the second, one, so one occurs. If he said 'except three', three occur because it is exception of the whole from the whole, so the exception is invalid. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on the validity of istithna (exception) in divorce pronouncements. The passage first addresses a scenario where the wife dies before the husband completes the conditional phrase 'in sha Allah'. The ruling states that divorce does not occur because the exception invalidates the declaration (ijab). It clarifies that death nullifies the person making the declaration, not the declaration itself; thus, if the wife dies before the full utterance, the declaration is void. However, if the husband dies after the declaration but before the exception, divorce occurs because the exception was not connected. The main ruling concerns exceptions in numbers of divorce. If a husband says 'you are divorced three except one', two divorces occur; 'except two' results in one divorce. The principle is that exception is speaking about what remains after the exception; it is valid only if some part remains and is connected to the original statement. Exception of the entire number (e.g., 'except three' when saying three) is invalid, and all three divorces take effect. The Hanafi school allows both small and large exceptions, contrary to the grammarian al-Farra' who did not permit exception of a small number. The reasoning is based on linguistic usage and continuity (ittisal).

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna): A grammatical exception using 'illa' (except) that removes some part from a general statement.
مستثنى منه (mustathna minhu): The whole from which the exception is made; in divorce, the total number of divorces stated.
اتصال (ittisal): The condition that the exception clause be uttered in immediate succession without a significant pause or intervening action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife 'Anti taliq thalathan illa wahidah', how many divorces occur?
A) Three divorces occur.
B) One divorce occurs.
C) Two divorces occur.
D) No divorce occurs.

Key Takeaway
An exception in divorce is valid only if it leaves some number remaining and is uttered without interruption; otherwise the full number takes effect.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Validity of Istithna in Talaq
Ruling with conditions of exception in divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid istithna in talaq and calculate the number of divorces that take effect after an exception.

Core Idea
An exception in talaq is valid only if it leaves something remaining and is connected to the original statement.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi position on making exceptions when pronouncing divorce. A husband may say 'I divorce you three times except one,' but what is the effect? The answer hinges on two conditions: the exception must leave a positive remainder, and it must be uttered without interruption. The text uses a simple analogy from debt to illustrate the logic underlying this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original statement and the exception
Note the number of divorces mentioned (the mustathna minhu) and the number excepted (the mustathna).
Example: 'You are divorced three except one' – original 3, except 1.
2
Calculate the remainder
Subtract the excepted number from the original. The remainder is the number of divorces that could take effect.
For 3 except 1, remainder = 2.
3
Check the first condition: remainder > 0
If the remainder is zero (whole-from-whole), the exception is invalid and the full original number of divorces occur.
Example: 3 except 3 → remainder 0 → exception invalid, 3 divorces occur.
4
Check the second condition: connection (mutassil)
The exception must be uttered immediately after the original statement without a significant pause.
If disconnected, the exception is invalid and the original pronouncement stands alone.
5
Apply the ruling
If both conditions are satisfied, the number of divorces that occur is the remainder. If either condition fails, the exception is void and the full original number of divorces are effective.
The ruling is based on linguistic principles and the need for certainty in the pronouncement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
۳۵۲
کتاب الطلاق
کثیر دونوں کا جائز ہے اگر چہ فرا نحوی نے اس کی اجازت نہیں دی ہے۔
استثناء کی اصل یہ ہے کہ استثناء کرنے کے بعد جو مقدار باقی رہی اس کا تکلم کرنا استثناء ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ مستثنی منہ کی جو مقدار باقی رہ گئی اس کا تکلم کرنا استثناء کہلائے گا۔ لہذا ایک آدمی کا قول کہ فلاں کا مجھ پر ایک درہم ہے اور اس کا قول کہ فلاں کے مجھ پر دس درہم ہیں نو کے علاوہ ان دونوں اقوال میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ پس حاصل یہ نکلا کہ کل سے بعض کا استثناء کرنا درست ہے۔ اور کل کا کل سے استثناء درست نہیں۔ کیونکہ کل کا استثناء کرنے کے بعد کچھ باقی نہیں رہے گا جس کے ساتھ تکلم کرنے والا ہو۔ اور استثناء کی صحت کیلئے یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ استثناء اصل کلام کے ساتھ متصل ہو۔
بہر حال جب یہ اصول ثابت ہو گیا تو پہلی صورت میں مستنئی منہ سے باقی ماندہ مقدار دو ہیں ۔ لہذا دو طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ اور دوسری صورت میں استثناء کے بعد باقی ماندہ ایک ہے۔ لہذا ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ اور اگر شوہر نے کہا انت طالق ثلاثاً الا ثلاثاً تو اس صورت میں استثناء باطل ہو گا۔ اور تین طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی ۔ کیونکہ یہ کل کا استثناء کل سے ہے۔ اور کل کا استثناء کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ استثناء کرنے کے بعد کوئی چیز باقی نہیں رہنی جس کے ساتھ اس کو تکلم کرنے والا کہا جائے۔ والله سبحانه و تعالى اعلم بالصواب
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Four. Kitab al-Talaq. Both are permissible even though Farra al-Nahwi did not permit it. The principle of exception is that after making an exception, the amount that remains is the exception. In other words, speaking of the amount that remains from the thing from which the exception is made is called exception. So there is no difference between a person's statement 'So-and-so owes me one dirham' and his statement 'So-and-so owes me ten dirhams except nine'. So the conclusion is that excepting a part from a whole is valid, and excepting a whole from a whole is not valid, because after excepting the whole, nothing remains for the speaker to speak of. For the validity of exception, it is also necessary that the exception be connected to the original speech. In any case, when this principle is established, then in the first case the remaining amount from the thing excepted from is two, so two divorces occur. In the second case, after the exception the remaining is one, so one divorce occurs. And if the husband said 'You are divorced three times except three', then in this case the exception is invalid and three divorces occur, because this is excepting the whole from the whole, and excepting the whole is not valid, because after making the exception nothing remains for the speaker to be considered speaking. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Hidayah's Book of Divorce, explaining the principle of istithna (exception) in divorce pronouncements. The author begins by stating the general rule: istithna is valid only when something remains after the exception. He provides an analogy from debt to illustrate: saying 'I owe ten dirhams except nine' is acceptable because one dirham remains as the subject of the speech. Similarly, in divorce, if a husband says 'I divorce you three times except two', then one divorce remains, so one divorce occurs. If he says 'except one', then two divorces occur. If he says 'except three', the exception is invalid because it leaves nothing, so all three divorces take effect. The text also mentions that the grammarian Farra al-Nahwi disagreed with this type of exception, but the Hanafi position is that it is valid as long as the exception is from a part to the whole (not whole to whole) and that the exception is connected (mutassil) to the original statement. The ruling is based on linguistic principles and logical reasoning.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna): In this passage, istithna refers to an exception made in a divorce pronouncement, where a part of the number is excluded from the total count.
متصل (mutassil): Connected, meaning the exception must be uttered immediately after the original statement without interruption.
مستثنیٰ منہ (mustathna minhu): The thing from which the exception is made, i.e., the total number of divorces mentioned before the exception (e.g., three in 'three except one').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced three times except two,' how many divorces occur?
A) 0
B) 1
C) 2
D) 3

Key Takeaway
An exception in talaq is valid only if it leaves at least one divorce remaining and is uttered immediately after the pronouncement.
